Refutation of Dualists Using Forgetfulness and Memory
Baqillani argues that forgetfulness and memory from one person refute dualist principles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the phenomenon of forgetfulness and memory in one person refutes the dualist claim that opposites require two distinct principles.

Core Idea
One person experiences both remembering and forgetting, proving a single substance can produce opposites.

Imam Baqillani presents a powerful argument against dualists who claim that opposites like light and darkness require two separate principles. He uses the everyday experience of forgetting where we put something to show that remembering and forgetting—clear opposites—come from the same human being. This simple observation, Baqillani argues, undermines the entire dualist framework.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and its translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the English translation to grasp the argument.
Focus on the logical flow from scenario to conclusion.
2
Identify the dualist claim being refuted
What do the dualists believe about opposites? They think opposites like light and darkness come from two different substances.
Baqillani is challenging this directly.
3
Understand Baqillani's argument
He gives an example of a person hiding something and forgetting. That same person later remembers. So both forgetfulness and memory come from one substance—the person himself.
This shows opposites can arise from one substance.
4
Consider the dualist objection and Baqillani's rebuttal
Dualists might say memory remains but is overcome by darkness. Baqillani rejects this because the person's own experience confirms he does not remember.
This appeal to sense experience and necessity is key.
5
Reflect on the broader implication
If one substance can produce opposites, then the dualist principle is false. Baqillani extends this to other opposites like cooling and heating.
The argument is decisive against dualism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُسألون أيضاً عمّن خبا شيئاً في موضع ونسيه وذهب عنه ذكره، فيقال لهم: أليس قد صار النَّاسي ذاكراً ووقع الذكر والنسيان مع اختلافهما من جوهر واحد فلِمَ لا يجوز أيضاً وقوع العدل والجور من جوهر واحد فإن قالوا: الواضعُ للشيء لم ينسَه وإنما غلبت عليه أجزاء الظلام وذكره باقٍ قائم يقال لهم: فالناسي إذاً للشيء بغلبة أجزاء الظلام عليه ذاكر له في حال نسيانه لأن ذكره عندكم موجود في هذه الحال وهذا دفع الحس والاضطرار لأن الإنسان يجد نفسه عند غلبة النسيان عليه غير ذاكر لما نسيه أصلاً ولا عالماً بموضعه وهذا يدلُّ على أن الذاكر قد يصيرُ ناسياً بعد الذكر وهو الذاكر نفسه وإن جاز ذلك جاز أن يصير المسخّنُ مبرداً والمبرد مسخّناً وهذا نقض قولهم.
And they are also asked about one who hid something in a place and forgot it and its memory left him. So it is said to them: has not the forgetter become a rememberer, and memory and forgetfulness occurred with their difference from one substance? So why is it not also permissible for justice and injustice to occur from one substance? If they say: the placer of the thing did not forget it, rather parts of darkness overcame him and his memory remains standing, it is said to them: then the forgetter of the thing, due to the overcoming of parts of darkness, is a rememberer of it in the state of his forgetfulness, because his memory, according to you, is present in this state. And this is a denial of sense and necessity, because a person finds himself, when forgetfulness overcomes him, not remembering what he forgot at all, nor knowing its place. And this indicates that the rememberer may become a forgetter after memory, and he is the same rememberer. And if that is permissible, it is permissible for the cooler to become a heater and the heater to become a cooler, and this is a refutation of their statement.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is another refutation of the dualists, using the everyday phenomenon of forgetfulness. Baqillani asks about a person who hides something and then forgets where it is. The dualists must admit that this same person goes from being a rememberer to being a forgetter, and that both remembering and forgetting come from one substance (the person himself). Therefore, consistency demands that justice and injustice can also come from one substance. The dualists might object that the person did not truly forget, but that darkness overtook him while his memory remains intact. Baqillani counters that this claim contradicts sense experience (الحس) and necessary knowledge (الاضطرار), because the person himself experiences not remembering anything about the hidden object. Thus, it is evident that the same substance can give rise to opposites. He concludes that if this is true, then a substance can be both cooling and heating at different times, which completely overturns the dualist position that two principles are necessary for opposites.

Key Terms
نسيان/ذكر (forgetfulness/memory)
جوهر واحد (one substance)
غلبة الظلام (overcoming of darkness)
حس (sense)
اضطرار (necessity)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Forgetfulness is due to external darkness overpowering an unchanged memory.
Correction: Direct experience shows that the person truly does not remember, so the memory is not intact.

Checkpoint
What is the dualists' claim about the person who forgets that Baqillani refutes?
A) The person actually remembers but is pretending.
B) The person's memory is overcome by darkness but still exists.
C) Forgetfulness is caused by a different substance.
D) The person is not the same substance after forgetting.

Key Takeaway
One person experiencing both forgetfulness and memory refutes the dualist claim that opposites require two distinct principles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever experienced forgetting something important and then later remembering? How does that personal experience confirm that your soul is a single entity capable of both memory and forgetfulness? How does that strengthen your conviction that God is one and can create both good and evil?
?
When you forget, do you ever blame external factors (like 'darkness' or distractions) instead of acknowledging your own state? How does this lesson call you to take responsibility for your own changes of heart and mind rather than attributing them to outside influences?
?
The argument hinges on the undeniable feeling of forgetfulness. In what area of your life are you currently making excuses for your own spiritual forgetfulness (e.g., blaming circumstances, people, or 'darkness')? What step will you take today to own your need to remember Allah and return to Him?

Magian Views on the Origin of Evil
Baqillani enumerates three Magian views on the devil's origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Magians were not monolithic but divided into sects with distinct theories about the origin of the devil.

Core Idea
Magians disagreed among themselves on how evil originated.

In this passage, Imam Baqillani opens a new chapter on the Magians, a dualist sect. Immediately, he demonstrates that they are not a single bloc but have at least three distinct explanations for the origin of the devil. This classification is crucial for the refutations that follow.

Guided Path
1
Read the chapter heading
Notice that Baqillani begins a new chapter titled 'باب الكلام على المجوس' (Chapter on the discourse concerning the Magians). This signals a shift in subject.
2
Identify the three groups
Read the list carefully. Baqillani mentions three groups: those who say the devil arose from a doubt in prayer, those who say from God's thought, and a third group whose view is cut off.
The third group is incomplete in this passage but introduced.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself why Baqillani begins with this classification. He is mapping the landscape of Magian views before refuting each one systematically.
This shows the method of Ahl al-Sunnah: understand the opponent's position accurately.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الكلام على المجوس القائلين بأن حدوث الشيطان من شكَّةٍ شكَّها شخص من أشخاص النور في صلاته والقائلين بأنه حدث من فكر الله تعالى والقائلين بأنه حدث
Chapter on the discourse concerning the Magians: Those who say that the occurrence of the devil came from a doubt that a person from the persons of light had in his prayer, and those who say that it occurred from the thought of God Most High, and those who say that it occurred

This passage is the beginning of a new chapter (باب) focusing on the Magians (المجوس), who are dualists but distinct from the earlier Manichaeans. Baqillani lists three groups among them based on their explanation of how the devil (الشيطان) or evil originated. The first group holds that the devil arose from a doubt (شكَّة) that occurred to a being of light during his prayer. The second group claims it originated from God's own thought (فكر الله). The third group is mentioned but the text cuts off mid-sentence ('and those who say that it occurred'), indicating that the list continues on later pages. This classification sets the stage for detailed refutations of each position.

?

?

?

Refuting Dualists: Memory and Forgetfulness as a Proof for Unity of Substance
Refutation of dualists through argument from memory and forgetfulness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the phenomenon of memory and forgetfulness in one person refutes the dualists' claim that opposites cannot arise from one substance.

Core Idea
If one person can both remember and forget, then one substance can produce justice and injustice.

Imam Baqillani presents a clever argument against the dualists who believe in two eternal principles. He uses a simple everyday experience—forgetting where you hid something—to show that opposites can indeed come from a single substance. This undermines their entire framework.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once. Notice the argument's structure: scenario, question, dualist reply, counter-argument, conclusion.
Pay attention to the experiential point at the end.
2
Identify the dualist claim
Dualists believe opposites require separate principles (light/darkness). Understand that this argument challenges that directly.
3
Follow the logical flow
Trace how Baqillani moves from a concrete example (hiding an object) to a general principle (opposites from one substance).
The dualist's attempted escape is refuted by pointing out that it contradicts direct experience.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The argument concludes that if opposites like memory/forgetfulness can arise from one substance, then so can justice/injustice. This destroys dualism.
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to see if you grasp the main point.
The activity will help solidify the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة في نقض آخر لجميع الثنوية تضادهما ويُسألون أيضاً عمّن خبا شيئاً في موضع ونسيه وذهب عنه ذكره، فيقال لهم : أليس قد صار النَّاسي ذاكراً ووقع الذكر والنسيان مع واختلافهما من جوهر واحد فلِمَ لا يجوز أيضاً وقوع العدل والجور من جوهر واحد فإن قالوا : الواضعُ للشيء لم ينسَه وإنما غلبت عليه أجزاء الظلام وذكره باقٍ قائم يقال لهم : فالناسي إذاً للشيء بغلبة أجزاء الظلام عليه ذاكر له في حال نسيانه لأن ذكره عندكم موجود في هذه الحال وهذا دفع الحس والاضطرار لأن الإنسان يجد نفسه عند غلبة النسيان عليه غير ذاكر لما نسيه أصلاً ولا عالماً بموضعه وهذا يدلُّ على أن الذاكر قد يصيرُ ناسياً بعد الذكر وهو الذاكر نفسه وإن جاز ذلك جاز أن يصير المسخّنُ مبرداً والمبرد مسخّناً وهذا نقض قولهم .
A question regarding another refutation of all the dualists. They are also asked about someone who hid something in a place and forgot it and his memory of it left him, so it is said to them: Has not the forgetful person become remembering? And memory and forgetfulness occur together and their difference [comes] from one substance? So why is it not also permissible that justice and injustice occur from one substance? If they say: The one who placed the thing did not forget it, but rather the parts of darkness overcame him and his memory remains established. It is said to them: So the forgetful person of the thing, due to the overcoming of the parts of darkness upon him, is remembering it in the state of his forgetfulness, because his memory, according to you, exists in this state. And this is a repudiation of sense and necessity, because a person finds himself, when forgetfulness overcomes him, not remembering what he forgot at all, nor knowing its location. And this indicates that the remembering person may become forgetful after memory, and he is the same remembering person. And if that is permissible, then it becomes permissible that the heater becomes a cooler and the cooler a heater, and this is a refutation of their statement.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage contains a refutation of the dualists (الثنوية) who posit two eternal principles (light and darkness). The argument proceeds in stages. First, the author poses a hypothetical: a man hides something and later forgets where he hid it. The dualists are asked: is it not the case that the forgetful person becomes remembering (i.e., the same person experiences both states)? And do not memory and forgetfulness arise from one substance (the same human essence)? If so, why cannot justice and injustice also arise from one substance? The dualists might reply that the person who hid the object did not truly forget—rather, the parts of darkness overwhelmed him, while his memory remains intact. The author counters: if that were true, then the forgetful person in that state would actually be remembering (since his memory, they claim, still exists). But this contradicts direct experience (دفع الحس والاضطرار). The person in the grip of forgetfulness finds himself entirely unaware of the forgotten thing. This proves that the same remembering person can become forgetful. If such a change is possible, then it is also possible for a heater to become a cooler and vice versa—an absurd consequence that refutes their dualistic framework.

Key Terms
نقض
ثنوية
ذاكر
ناسي
جوهر
عدل
جور
جزاء الظلام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The dualists claim that opposites cannot arise from one substance, and that forgetfulness is just domination by darkness.
Correction: The argument shows that forgetfulness is a real change in the same person, proving that one substance can produce opposites.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the refutation against the dualists in this passage?
A) Memory and forgetfulness cannot occur in one substance.
B) If opposites like memory/forgetfulness can come from one substance, then justice/injustice can too.
C) Darkness overcomes memory completely, so justice is impossible.
D) The forgetful person is always still remembering.

Key Takeaway
The experience of memory and forgetfulness in one person proves that a single substance can produce opposites, refuting dualism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have experienced both remembering and forgetting in your own life. When you forget something important, do you ever blame external factors (like stress or lack of sleep) rather than accepting your own fallibility? How does this passage challenge you to own your own nature, including its weaknesses?
?
The dualists tried to separate good and evil into two independent sources. Reflect on a time when you committed a wrong action and found yourself attributing it to a part of yourself that is 'not the real you.' In light of this lesson, is that a true separation, or an excuse? How can you take full responsibility for both your good and bad choices?
?
The argument ends with the absurd idea that a heater could become a cooler. What is a 'dualistic' belief in your own heart that, if examined, would lead to a similar absurdity? For example, believing your faith can be strong while your actions are weak? How does this proof push you to seek consistency in your character?

Magian Views on Shaytan's Origin and Their Refutation
Enumeration of three Magian views and their refutation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three Magian beliefs about the origin of Shaytan and the rational refutation based on God's eternal knowledge and transcendence.

Core Idea
God's eternal knowledge precludes any thought, doubt, or ignorance.

Before we engage with specific sects, we need to see how Muslim theologians argued against claims that seem to attribute imperfection to God. The Magians (Zoroastrians) proposed various origins for the devil that implied God had thoughts, doubts, or punishing actions that led to creation. This passage introduces those views and provides a crisp refutation rooted in God's transcendence. Let's read the original Arabic and unpack its logic.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once without analysis. Let the structure of the chapter heading and the three views sink in. Then read the translation.
The passage is a miniature argument: three views, an objection, and an answer.
2
Identify the three Magian views
Find the three phrases starting with 'القائلين بأن' and note each supposed cause of the devil's occurrence: doubt, thought, punishment.
These are presented as beliefs of the Magians.
3
Understand the objection
The text then raises a possible question from a Magian: why deny that God's act could come from thought, doubt, or punishment? See how the objection is phrased.
4
Analyze the refutation
The answer states that thought and doubt are impossible for the Eternal (al-Qadim), just as ignorance is. Reflect on why this is a powerful argument.
The refutation is concise and relies on a fundamental attribute of God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الكلام على المجوس القائلين بأن حدوث الشيطان من شكّةٍ شكّها شخص من أشخاص النور في صلاته والقائلين بأنه حدث من فكر الله تعالى والقائلين بأنه حدث من عقوبة عاقب الله بها سبحانه وتعالى . هو الشيطان إن قال منهم قائل ؛ لِمَ أنكرتم أن يحدث فعل الله من أو غيره من فكرة فكرها أو شكة شكّها أو عقوبة عاقب بها؟ قيل له : لقيام الدليل على استحالة الفكر والشَّكُ على القديم كما يستحيل عليه الجهل
Chapter on the discussion of the Magians: those who say that the occurrence of the devil was from a doubt that a person among the persons of light doubted in his prayer, and those who say that he occurred from a thought of God Almighty, and those who say that he occurred from a punishment with which God, glorified and exalted, punished. [It is said:] He is the devil. If a speaker among them says: Why do you deny that an act of God occurs from a thought He thought, or a doubt He doubted, or a punishment He punished? It is said to him: Because the proof stands for the impossibility of thought and doubt for the Eternal, just as ignorance is impossible for Him.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage opens a chapter (باب) on the Magians (المجوس). It lists three of their views on the origin of the devil (الشيطان): (1) that he arose from a doubt that a person among the light-entities doubted during prayer, (2) that he arose from a thought of God (فكر الله), and (3) that he arose from a punishment inflicted by God. The text then presents a potential objection: a Magian might ask why Muslims deny that an act of God could originate from a thought, doubt, or punishment. The reply is that it is impossible for God—the Eternal (القديم)—to have thought or doubt, just as it is impossible for Him to have ignorance. This is a concise theological refutation based on divine transcendence: God's knowledge is eternal and perfect, so He does not need to think or doubt, and He does not act from such imperfections.

Key Terms
مجوس
شيطان
شك
فكر
عقوبة
قديم
جهل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument denies that God can will evil or create evil beings.
Correction: The argument does not deny that God can will evil; it denies that God has thought or doubt as intellectual processes that imply prior ignorance. Thought and doubt are imperfections, not acts of will.

Checkpoint
Why does the author reject the Magian claim that the devil could originate from a thought of God?
A) Because thought implies ignorance, and God is not ignorant.
B) Because the devil is not a creature of God.
C) Because God only creates good things.
D) Because thought is impossible for any being.

Key Takeaway
God's eternal knowledge makes thought, doubt, and ignorance impossible for Him, refuting any Magian claims that the devil originated from such processes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever pictured God 'thinking' about something as if He were a human who sometimes knows and sometimes learns? How does this passage challenge that picture, and what must you renew in your heart to truly believe in His eternal knowledge?
?
When you face confusion or doubt about God's decree, do you unconsciously attribute ignorance or indecision to Him? What specific thought will you recall from this lesson the next time such doubt arises?
?
If God's knowledge is perfect and unchanging, then every event in your life is known from eternity. Does that comfort you or unsettle you? How can you train yourself to live with complete trust in that eternal knowledge, even when you don't understand His timing?

The Dialectic on the Origin of Shaytan: Eternal or Uncaused?
Baqillani opens his refutation by questioning the ontological status of Shaytan's origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes the Magian claim that Shaytan's origin is either eternal or uncaused, exposing the logical absurdities that follow.

Core Idea
If Shaytan's origin is eternal, Shaytan is eternal; if uncaused, all events are uncaused.

Baqillani begins by posing a simple question to the Magians: is the origin of Shaytan (doubt, thought, or punishment) eternal or created? He then shows that both answers lead to contradictions. This lesson traces the first two branches of the argument, where the Magians are forced to either accept the eternity of Shaytan or deny the existence of a Creator.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening question
Read the Arabic passage from the start. Notice the direct address to the Magians and the binary choice presented: is the origin eternal or created?
This sets up the entire dialectic.
2
Examine the eternal origin branch
If the Magians say the origin is eternal, Baqillani argues that this implies the eternity of ignorance and forces Shaytan to be eternal. Understand the causal link.
The key is that the effect follows the cause.
3
Examine the created origin branch (no creator)
If the Magians say the origin is created but not by a creator, then all events could be uncaused, leading to atheism (ta'til). See how Baqillani exposes this consequence.
4
Summarize the refutations
Both options lead to unacceptable conclusions. The Magians are left with no escape. Reflect on the strength of this dialectical approach.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة في نقض المجوس ثم يقال لهم خبرونا عن الشك أو التفكر أو العقوبة التي حدث منها الشيطان أمحدت ذلك أم قديم فإن قالوا بقدم هذه الأمور ألزموا إحالة كون الباري عالما وأوجب عليهم قدم الجهل ثم قيل لهم فإن كان الشك والفكر والعقوبة التي عنها كان الشيطان قديمة فما أنكرتم أن يكون الشيطان قديما لقدم ما كان عنه فإن مروا على ذلك تركوا قولهم بحدوثه ولا خلاص لهم من ذلك وإن قالوا إن الشك محدث وكذلك العقوبة والفكر عند القائل بكل واحد منهما قيل لهم أفمن محدث حدث الشك أم لا من محدث فإن قالوا لا من محدث قيل لهم فما يؤمنكم أن يكون سائر الأفعال والحوادث كائنة لا من محدث وفي ذلك التعطيل وإبطال الصانع وإن قالوا من محدث حدثت هذه الأمور قيل لهم فمن محدثها فإن قالوا الشيطان تجاهلوا وقيل لهم فقد كان الشيطان قبل الفكر والشك اللذين كان عنهما فكيف يكون الشيء قبل أصله وسببه الذي عنه كان ووجد وإن قالوا الله أحدث الشك والفكرة قيل لهم فخبرونا عن الشك والفكرة أشر هما أم خير فإن قالوا خير قيل لهم فكيف كان عنهما الشيطان الذي هو شر وما أنكرتم إن جاز ذلك أن يفكر الشيطان الذي هو شر فكرا هو شر يتولد عنه ويقع الخير وإن جاز ذلك جاز وقوع التبريد عن النار والتسخين عن الثلج وهذا نقض قولهم وإن قالوا إن الشك شر لأنه ولد الشيطان الذي هو شر قيل لهم فقد فعل الله الخير الشك الذي هو شر من الشر وهو أصل الشيطان وإن جاز ذلك فلم لا يجوز أن يفعل سائر الشرور وجميع الأشخاص الضارة من السباع والعقارب والحيات والهموم والأحزان وسائر الشرور وما الفصل في ذلك ولا فصل فيه
A question concerning refuting the Magians. Then it is said to them: 'Tell us about the doubt, thought, or punishment from which Shaytan occurred—are these created or eternal?' If they say that these matters are eternal, they are forced into the impossibility of the Creator being knowing and they are obliged to accept the eternity of ignorance. Then it is said to them: 'If the doubt, thought, and punishment from which Shaytan was are eternal, then what prevents you from saying that Shaytan is eternal due to the eternity of that from which he was?' If they pass over that, they abandon their statement of his temporality, and they have no escape from that. And if they say that doubt is created, and likewise punishment and thought according to the one who says each, it is said to them: 'Does doubt occur from a creator or not from a creator?' If they say 'not from a creator,' it is said to them: 'What assurance do you have that all other acts and events occur without a creator? And in that is denial and nullification of the Maker.' If they say 'from a creator' these things occurred, it is said to them: 'Who is their creator?' If they say 'Shaytan,' they feign ignorance, and it is said to them: 'Then Shaytan existed before the thought and doubt from which he was; how can a thing exist before its origin and cause from which it was and came to be?' And if they say 'God created doubt and thought,' it is said to them: 'Tell us about doubt and thought—are they evil or good?' If they say 'good,' it is said to them: 'How then did Shaytan, who is evil, occur from them? And what prevents you, if that is permissible, that Shaytan, who is evil, thinks an evil thought that generates good and good occurs? And if that is permissible, then it would be permissible for cooling to occur from fire and heating from snow. This refutes their statement.' And if they say that doubt is evil because it generated Shaytan who is evil, it is said to them: 'Then God has done good by creating doubt, which is evil from evil, and it is the origin of Shaytan. And if that is permissible, why is it not permissible for Him to do all other evils and all harmful entities like beasts, scorpions, snakes, worries, sorrows, and all other evils? And what is the distinction in that? There is no distinction in it.'
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This is a detailed dialectical refutation of the Magian (مجوس) claim that Shaytan originated from doubt, thought, or punishment. Bāqillānī systematically examines each possible answer the opponent might give, showing that each leads to an absurd consequence. The argument proceeds as follows: (1) If they say these origins are eternal, then Shaytan would be eternal (since effect follows cause), contradicting their claim that he is created. (2) If they say these origins are created, then either they have a creator or not. If no creator, then all events could be uncaused, which is atheism (تعطيل). If they have a creator and they say it is Shaytan, then Shaytan would exist before his own origin (impossible). If they say God is the creator, then either the origins are good or evil. If good, then how can evil come from good? That would also allow absurd reversals like fire cooling. If the origins are evil, then God created evil, and He might as well create all evils, which they must admit—thus no distinction can be made. The passage ends with the conclusion that there is no valid distinction (لا فصل فيه).

Key Terms
نقض المجوس
الشك
التفكر
العقوبة
قدم
حدوث
التعطيل
إبطال الصانع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if the origin is created, it automatically has a creator.
Correction: Baqillani considers the possibility that the Magians might deny a creator for the origin, forcing them into atheism.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if the Magians say the origin of Shaytan (doubt) is eternal?
A) Shaytan must also be eternal.
B) Doubt must be good.
C) The creator is eternal.
D) All events are uncaused.

Key Takeaway
The Magians cannot claim the origin of Shaytan is either eternal or uncaused without falling into absurdity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a belief about the world that contradicts clear Islamic teachings, do you honestly follow the logical consequences wherever they lead, or do you look for comfortable 'escape routes'? What is one belief you have held that you need to re-examine in light of this dilemma?
?
The Magians were forced to admit that their view led to either an eternal Shaytan or a world without a Creator. Have you ever held a position that, if logically pressed, would undermine your own tawheed? What will you do today to ensure your beliefs are consistent with the fact that Allah is the sole Creator of all things?
?
Baqillani's argument leaves no middle ground: either Shaytan's origin is eternal (making him a partner with Allah) or created (requiring a Creator). Which side do you stand on, and are you willing to defend it with clear reasoning? If not, what step will you take to strengthen your certainty?

The Dilemma of the Creator: Good or Evil Origin?
Baqillani continues his refutation by examining the creator of the origin and the good/evil nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes the Magian claims that Shaytan's origin is created by Shaytan or by God, and the logical consequences regarding good and evil.

Core Idea
If God created the origin, it must be good or evil, and both options lead to absurdities.

After showing that the origin cannot be eternal or uncaused, Baqillani turns to the possibility that the origin was created by a creator. He then examines two sub-possibilities: the creator is Shaytan himself, or the creator is God. Both lead to contradictions, especially when analyzing whether the origin is good or evil.

Guided Path
1
Read the continuation of the argument
Read from 'وإن قالوا من محدث' to the end. Notice how Baqillani deals with each response.
2
Analyze the claim that Shaytan created his own origin
If Shaytan created the doubt/thought that caused him, then he would exist before his own cause, which is impossible.
This is a logical contradiction.
3
Analyze the claim that God created the origin
Now Baqillani asks whether the origin is good or evil. If good, then good produces evil, which is absurd. If evil, then God created evil, and there is no reason to limit His creation of evil.
Note the reductio ad absurdum with fire cooling and snow heating.
4
Conclude the refutation
Baqillani ends by stating that there is no valid distinction (لا فصل فيه) — the Magian position collapses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة في نقض المجوس ثم يقال لهم خبرونا عن الشك أو التفكر أو العقوبة التي حدث منها الشيطان أمحدت ذلك أم قديم فإن قالوا بقدم هذه الأمور ألزموا إحالة كون الباري عالما وأوجب عليهم قدم الجهل ثم قيل لهم فإن كان الشك والفكر والعقوبة التي عنها كان الشيطان قديمة فما أنكرتم أن يكون الشيطان قديما لقدم ما كان عنه فإن مروا على ذلك تركوا قولهم بحدوثه ولا خلاص لهم من ذلك وإن قالوا إن الشك محدث وكذلك العقوبة والفكر عند القائل بكل واحد منهما قيل لهم أفمن محدث حدث الشك أم لا من محدث فإن قالوا لا من محدث قيل لهم فما يؤمنكم أن يكون سائر الأفعال والحوادث كائنة لا من محدث وفي ذلك التعطيل وإبطال الصانع وإن قالوا من محدث حدثت هذه الأمور قيل لهم فمن محدثها فإن قالوا الشيطان تجاهلوا وقيل لهم فقد كان الشيطان قبل الفكر والشك اللذين كان عنهما فكيف يكون الشيء قبل أصله وسببه الذي عنه كان ووجد وإن قالوا الله أحدث الشك والفكرة قيل لهم فخبرونا عن الشك والفكرة أشر هما أم خير فإن قالوا خير قيل لهم فكيف كان عنهما الشيطان الذي هو شر وما أنكرتم إن جاز ذلك أن يفكر الشيطان الذي هو شر فكرا هو شر يتولد عنه ويقع الخير وإن جاز ذلك جاز وقوع التبريد عن النار والتسخين عن الثلج وهذا نقض قولهم وإن قالوا إن الشك شر لأنه ولد الشيطان الذي هو شر قيل لهم فقد فعل الله الخير الشك الذي هو شر من الشر وهو أصل الشيطان وإن جاز ذلك فلم لا يجوز أن يفعل سائر الشرور وجميع الأشخاص الضارة من السباع والعقارب والحيات والهموم والأحزان وسائر الشرور وما الفصل في ذلك ولا فصل فيه
A question concerning refuting the Magians. Then it is said to them: 'Tell us about the doubt, thought, or punishment from which Shaytan occurred—are these created or eternal?' If they say that these matters are eternal, they are forced into the impossibility of the Creator being knowing and they are obliged to accept the eternity of ignorance. Then it is said to them: 'If the doubt, thought, and punishment from which Shaytan was are eternal, then what prevents you from saying that Shaytan is eternal due to the eternity of that from which he was?' If they pass over that, they abandon their statement of his temporality, and they have no escape from that. And if they say that doubt is created, and likewise punishment and thought according to the one who says each, it is said to them: 'Does doubt occur from a creator or not from a creator?' If they say 'not from a creator,' it is said to them: 'What assurance do you have that all other acts and events occur without a creator? And in that is denial and nullification of the Maker.' If they say 'from a creator' these things occurred, it is said to them: 'Who is their creator?' If they say 'Shaytan,' they feign ignorance, and it is said to them: 'Then Shaytan existed before the thought and doubt from which he was; how can a thing exist before its origin and cause from which it was and came to be?' And if they say 'God created doubt and thought,' it is said to them: 'Tell us about doubt and thought—are they evil or good?' If they say 'good,' it is said to them: 'How then did Shaytan, who is evil, occur from them? And what prevents you, if that is permissible, that Shaytan, who is evil, thinks an evil thought that generates good and good occurs? And if that is permissible, then it would be permissible for cooling to occur from fire and heating from snow. This refutes their statement.' And if they say that doubt is evil because it generated Shaytan who is evil, it is said to them: 'Then God has done good by creating doubt, which is evil from evil, and it is the origin of Shaytan. And if that is permissible, why is it not permissible for Him to do all other evils and all harmful entities like beasts, scorpions, snakes, worries, sorrows, and all other evils? And what is the distinction in that? There is no distinction in it.'
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This is a detailed dialectical refutation of the Magian (مجوس) claim that Shaytan originated from doubt, thought, or punishment. Bāqillānī systematically examines each possible answer the opponent might give, showing that each leads to an absurd consequence. The argument proceeds as follows: (1) If they say these origins are eternal, then Shaytan would be eternal (since effect follows cause), contradicting their claim that he is created. (2) If they say these origins are created, then either they have a creator or not. If no creator, then all events could be uncaused, which is atheism (تعطيل). If they have a creator and they say it is Shaytan, then Shaytan would exist before his own origin (impossible). If they say God is the creator, then either the origins are good or evil. If good, then how can evil come from good? That would also allow absurd reversals like fire cooling. If the origins are evil, then God created evil, and He might as well create all evils, which they must admit—thus no distinction can be made. The passage ends with the conclusion that there is no valid distinction (لا فصل فيه).

Key Terms
الشيطان
الشر
الخير
التبريد
التسخين
لا فصل فيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if God creates the origin of evil, He is unjust.
Correction: Baqillani does not address justice here; rather, he uses the opponent's own logic to show inconsistency.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if the Magians say that doubt is good?
A) Then Shaytan must be good too.
B) Then good generates evil, which leads to absurdities like fire cooling.
C) Then doubt must be eternal.
D) Then God is not all-powerful.

Key Takeaway
The Magian position on the origin of Shaytan collapses under logical scrutiny, with no coherent option remaining.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself blaming Shaytan for your evil thoughts, does this passage challenge you to take personal responsibility? Where in your life are you evading ownership of your own doubts?
?
The argument shows that claiming God created one evil but not others is logically arbitrary. In your own heart, do you sometimes pick and choose which sins to excuse as 'natural' while condemning others? How does this reflect on your view of God's justice?
?
If you believe God is the creator of all things, including the capacity for evil in your own soul, how does this lesson reshape your understanding of His will? Are you willing to accept that He may have purposes beyond your moral categories?

Questioning the Punishment Theory and Divine Origin of Evil
Bāqillānī questions those who claim Shaytan originated from a punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Bāqillānī uses a regress argument to question those who claim Shaytan arose from divine punishment, exposing a theological inconsistency.

Core Idea
If God creates the sinner, He is ultimately the source of evil.

In this passage, Bāqillānī confronts a particular theological view that claims Shaytan came into existence as a punishment from God. He poses a simple yet penetrating question: who created the disobedient person who deserved that punishment? If the answer is God, then God is implicated in the evil of disobedience just as much as the sinner. This lesson unpacks the logic of that challenge.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the rhetorical question at the end.
2
Understand the opponent's claim
Identify the opponents Bāqillānī addresses: the 'proponents of thought and punishment.' They believe that Shaytan originated as a result of a punishment from God.
This sets up the target of the argument.
3
Trace the regress
Follow the question: 'Who created the disobedient one deserving punishment?' If the answer is God, then God is the source of the evil (disobedience). The rhetorical question forces the opponent to see that God is implicated in evil.
This is the core of the argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك السؤال على أصحاب الفكر والعقاب ويقال للقائلين بأن الشيطان حدث عن عقوبة من خلق العاصي المستوجب للعقاب فإذا قالوا الله قيل لهم أفليس من كان منه العصيان شرا كالذي كان منه
And likewise the question is posed to the proponents of thought and punishment. And it is said to those who say that Shaytan occurred from a punishment: 'Who created the disobedient one deserving of punishment?' If they say 'God,' it is said to them: 'Is not the one from whom disobedience comes evil, like the one from whom it came?'
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage applies a similar line of reasoning to those who claim that Shaytan originated from a punishment imposed by God. Bāqillānī asks: if Shaytan came from a punishment, then who created the disobedient person who deserved that punishment? If the answer is God, then God is the ultimate source of the disobedience that led to the punishment and ultimately to Shaytan. This implies that God is responsible for evil in the same way as the one who directly committed disobedience. The question highlights an inconsistency: if God creates the evildoer, then He is implicated in evil, which the opponent likely denies. The argument is left as a challenge, expecting the opponent to find no valid distinction.

Key Terms
السؤال
أصحاب الفكر والعقاب
عقوبة
العاصي
العصيان
شر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the punishment is independent of God's creation, so God is not responsible for the evil that leads to punishment.
Correction: Bāqillānī traces the chain back to God: since God created the disobedient person, He is the ultimate source of the evil (disobedience) that led to the punishment.

Checkpoint
What dilemma does Bāqillānī present to proponents of the punishment theory?
A) If God created the sinner, then God is the source of evil.
B) If Shaytan was punished, he must have sinned before being created.
C) Punishment is eternal and uncreated.
D) The punishment cannot be an accident.

Key Takeaway
Bāqillānī's question shows that if God creates the sinner, then God is the ultimate source of evil, which undermines the claim that Shaytan arose from a punishment without divine responsibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness or experience evil in your life, do you instinctively blame the immediate agent or do you trace it back to God's ultimate will? How would this lesson change your response?
?
If you truly believe that God is the creator of all actions, including disobedience, can you still hold Him blameless for the evil in the world? What does that mean for your trust in His justice?
?
Bāqillānī's argument forces you to admit that if God creates the disobedient, then He is the source of evil. Does this thought disturb your faith, or does it drive you to a deeper understanding of God's wisdom beyond human categories? What will you do with this discomfort?

Baqillani's Dialectical Refutation of the Magians on Shaytan
Baqillani questions the Magians on shaytan's origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses a dilemma to argue that the Magian dualistic position on shaytan leads to the same conclusion that God creates evil, thereby refuting their dualism.

Core Idea
Dualism cannot escape the conclusion that God creates evil.

Baqillani engages the Magians on their own ground, asking a simple question about shaytan. Through a series of forced choices, he reveals that whether they claim shaytan is eternal or originated, they end up contradicting their core beliefs. This dialogue demonstrates a classic method of refutation by dilemma.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without stopping. Then read the translation. Notice the back-and-forth structure of the argument.
Baqillani uses very direct questions; imagine the debate.
2
Identify the key dilemma
Find the two options Baqillani presents about shaytan: eternal or originated. Trace the consequences of each.
The Magians cannot accept either without giving up their dualism.
3
Analyze the consequence chain
If originated, follow the further question about the originator. Baqillani forces them to admit God as originator.
4
Understand the final conclusion
The passage ends with the conclusion that God creates evil and is wise. This destroys the Magian claim that evil cannot come from God.
The phrase 'لا فصل في هذا' means there is no distinction between good and evil in this regard.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة أخرى في نقض المجوس، وكذلك يسألون فيقال لهم : خبرونا عن الشيطان : أمحدّث هو عندكم أم قديم؟ فإن قالوا قديم تركوا قولهم وإن قالوا محدث، قيل لهم : أفمن محدث حدث أم لا من محدث؟ فإن قالوا : لا من محدث قيل لهم : فما أنكرتم من وقوع الحوادث لا من محدث؟ وإن قالوا من محدث قيل لهم : ومَن محدثه؟ فإن قالوا الله سبحانه ولا بد من ذلك، قيل لهم : فما أنكرتم أن يُحدث الباري سبحانه سائر الشرور ويكون بذلك حكيماً غير سفيه؟ ولا فصل في هذا .
Another issue in refuting the Magians. And likewise they are asked, and it is said to them: 'Inform us about shaytan: is it originated (muhdath) in your view or eternal (qadim)?' If they say eternal, they abandon their statement. And if they say originated, it is said to them: 'Is it from an originator or not from an originator?' If they say: 'Not from an originator,' it is said to them: 'What prevents you from the occurrence of events without an originator?' And if they say: 'From an originator,' it is said to them: 'And who originated it?' If they say: 'God, exalted, and there is no alternative,' it is said to them: 'What prevents you from [admitting] that the Creator (al-Bari), exalted, creates all evils and thereby is wise, not foolish? There is no distinction in this.'
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Magian dualists. Baqillani forces them into a dilemma about shaytan: either it is eternal, which would contradict their belief in two eternal principles (since they likely only attribute eternity to light), or it is originated. If originated, then either it came from no originator (leading to no creator) or from an originator. If from an originator, that originator must be God. Consequently, God creates evils, which they deny. Thus, they cannot avoid the conclusion that God creates evil, or else they must accept the consequence of no originator.

Key Terms
المجوس (al-majus: Magians)
قديم (qadim: eternal)
محدث (muhdath: originated)
محدث (muhdith: originator)
الباري (al-Bari: the Creator)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That dualism (believing in two eternal principles of good and evil) avoids the problem of evil because evil is attributed to an independent power.
Correction: Baqillani shows that even in dualism, the devil (evil) must be either eternal or originated. If eternal, it conflicts with the dualist's own system. If originated, it must be from an originator, who is God, thus God is the creator of evil.

Checkpoint
What is the immediate consequence if the Magians say shaytan is eternal?
A) They admit shaytan is from an originator.
B) They abandon their own statement (contradiction).
C) They accept that God creates evil.
D) They deny the existence of evil.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani's dilemma forces the Magians to admit that God is the originator of shaytan and thus the creator of all evil, which they cannot differentiate from good.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face evil or suffering in your own life, do you instinctively question God's wisdom or goodness? How does this lesson's claim that God creates all evil and remains wise challenge your immediate reaction? Will you commit to trusting His wisdom even when you cannot see the good?
?
What 'Shaytans' in your life—people, circumstances, or your own desires—do you tend to blame as independent sources of evil, separate from God's decree? Will you now acknowledge that every trial comes from Him and respond with patience and gratitude?
?
If dualism is false and God alone is the originator of all things, including evil, then what comfort or excuse do you have for your own sins? Can you still claim that 'the devil made me do it' or that external forces override your responsibility? Will you own your actions before God and seek His forgiveness?

Cross-Refuting Internal Disagreements: The Origin of Shaytan
Baqillani uses one group's claim to refute another's on the devil's origin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the internal contradictions among various groups to refute their claims about the origin of the devil.

Core Idea
One group's claim refutes another's: internal disagreement invalidates erroneous theories.

Baqillani demonstrates a powerful refutation method: he does not need to disprove each heretical group individually. Instead, he shows that their own contradictory claims cancel each other out. This passage illustrates how the disagreements among those who speculate about the origin of shaytan actually serve as evidence against all of them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the refutation structure.
2
Identify the four claims
The passage mentions four different proposed origins: persons of light, thought, doubt, and punishment.
3
Follow the refutation chain
Notice how each claim is used to counter the previous one, forming a chain of mutual refutations.
4
Understand the strategy
Recognize that Baqillani is not endorsing any of these views; he is exposing their inconsistency.
This is a common polemical technique.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويعارض من قال : إن الشيطان حدث أشخاص النور بقول من قال : حدث عن فكرة ؛ ويعارض أهلُ الفكر بأصحاب الشَّكُ ؛ ويعارَضُ الفريقان بقول أصحاب العقاب.
And it is countered against the one who says that shaytan originated from the persons of light (ashkhas al-nur) by the statement of the one who says 'it originated from thought (or idea)'; and the adherents of thought are countered by the adherents of doubt; and the two groups are countered by the statement of the adherents of punishment.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This short passage presents a refutation strategy: Baqillani uses the claims of one group against another. Those who say shaytan originated from 'persons of light' (i.e., from the good principle) are refuted by those who say it originated from 'thought'. The latter group (adherents of thought) are refuted by those who say from 'doubt'. And both groups together are refuted by those who say from 'punishment'. Thus, their internal disagreements invalidate their positions, as each can be used against the other.

Key Terms
أشخاص النور (ashkhas al-nur: persons of light)
الفكرة (al-fikra: thought/idea)
الشك (al-shakk: doubt)
العقاب (al-uquba: punishment)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These are separate valid theories about the origin of shaytan.
Correction: Baqillani does not present them as valid; he shows they contradict each other, thus refuting all of them.

Checkpoint
How does Baqillani refute the different groups regarding the origin of shaytan?
A) By proving each is false independently.
B) By using one group's claim to refute another's.
C) By appealing to scripture.
D) By denying the existence of shaytan.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes multiple heretical groups by using their own contradictory claims against each other.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter disagreements among people who oppose the truth, do you feel confusion or confidence? This lesson shows that their contradictions expose their falsehood. Will you let this strengthen your trust in the truth you hold, or will you allow their noise to shake you?
?
Have you ever accepted a belief without checking if it contradicts other things you hold true? This passage warns that inconsistency is a sign of falsehood. Are you willing to examine your own beliefs for hidden contradictions, even if it is uncomfortable?
?
Baqillani uses the opponents' own words against them. Do you know the claims of falsehood well enough to refute them? Or have you avoided learning about opposing views? Commit today to learn at least one false argument so you can respond with truth.

Baqillani's Challenge to Magian Dualism
Baqillani challenges Magians on the eternity of darkness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses a logical parity argument to challenge the Magian belief in the eternity of both light and darkness.

Core Idea
If light is eternal, why not darkness?

In dealing with dualist sects like the Magians, kalam theologians often used parity arguments. Baqillani here confronts the Magian claim that light is eternal (and identified with God) while darkness is not. He challenges them to explain why darkness could not also be eternal if light can be. This passage shows a key method: forcing the opponent to justify their distinctions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it. Then read the translation. Let Baqillani's rhetorical question sink in.
The passage is short but pregnant with argument.
2
Identify the logical structure
Ask yourself: What assumption does Baqillani grant the Magians? What consequence does he draw? Why is this question difficult for them?
The argument is a reductio ad absurdum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة في نقض المجوس أيضاً ، ويقال لهم : إذا جاز قِدَم النور الذي هو الباري ، فما أنكرتم من قدم الشيطان الذي هو ظلام؟ فإن تعاطوا إقامة الدليل على حدث الظلام بشيء،
A issue in refuting the Magians as well. And it is said to them: 'If the eternity of light (al-nur), which is the Creator (al-Bari), is allowed, what prevents you from the eternity of shaytan, which is darkness (zalam)? Then if they attempt to adduce evidence for the temporality of darkness with something...'
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage challenges the Magian dualism of light and darkness. Baqillani argues that if light (identified with God) is eternal, then there is no reason to deny the eternity of darkness. If they try to prove darkness is temporally originated (i.e., created), they will face difficulties. The argument is left incomplete in this window, but the challenge is clear: they cannot consistently maintain the eternity of light while denying the eternity of darkness without a decisive proof that darkness is originated.

Key Terms
النور (al-nur: light)
الظلام (al-zalam: darkness)
قِدَم (qidam: eternity)
الباري (al-Bari: the Creator)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That light and darkness are coeternal and independent principles.
Correction: Baqillani does not assert that both are eternal; rather, he argues that if the Magians claim light is eternal, they must explain why darkness is not also eternal, exposing an inconsistency in their dualism.

Checkpoint
What is Baqillani's challenge to the Magians about darkness?
A) That darkness is not real.
B) That if light is eternal, why should darkness not be eternal?
C) That darkness is more powerful than light.
D) That darkness was created by light.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani exposes an inconsistency in Magian dualism by using a parity argument: if light (God) is eternal, there is no obvious reason to deny the eternity of darkness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what areas of your life do you apply a double standard—holding others to a rule you don't follow yourself? Baqillani's challenge forces you to face inconsistency. Will you examine one such area today and commit to change?
?
You believe in the Oneness of God (tawhid). But do you ever act as if something else—money, status, comfort—has equal or greater claim to your ultimate allegiance? If Baqillani asked you about that 'other eternal,' what would you say?
?
The Magians couldn't justify treating darkness differently from light. Can you justify the gaps between what you profess and how you live? This lesson demands consistency between belief and action. What is one small step you will take today to close that gap?

The Dilemma of the Liar and the Origin of Evil
Baqillani poses a dilemma about who creates a liar claiming to be from Satan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses a dilemma about a liar claiming to be from Satan to refute the dualist division of good and evil.

Core Idea
A single liar exposes the impossibility of separate sources for good and evil.

This passage presents a sharp dialectical objection against those who believe in two eternal principles: light (good) and darkness (evil). The author constructs a dilemma around a man who claims 'I am from the creation of Satan.' Whichever answer the dualist gives, it forces a contradiction that undermines their core doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to get the flow of the argument.
Notice the direct style: 'inform us about one whom we have heard say...'
2
Understand the dualist context
Recall that dualists (like Manichaeans) believe light (good) and darkness (evil) are separate, eternal principles. This objection targets that separation.
The word 'نور' refers to the good principle.
3
Analyze the first horn: if light created him
If the dualists say light created the man, then light would have created a liar (since he falsely claims to be from Satan) and someone who misattributes his own creation. This forces light to be capable of creating evil, collapsing the distinction.
The text: 'فقد خَلَقَ النُّورِ مَن كَذِبَ'
4
Analyze the second horn: if Satan created him
If they say Satan created the man, then the man is truthful (since he correctly attributes himself to Satan). This means Satan created a truthful good act, implying Satan can create good. Why then deny that all good comes from Satan? This also collapses the separation.
The text: 'فقد صَدَقَ هذا الناطق'
5
Reflect on the conclusion
The author concludes 'وهذا ترك دينكم' – this is abandoning your religion. The dilemma forces the dualist to abandon the core tenet of two separate sources.
Consider how a single, well-constructed dilemma can dismantle a whole worldview.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة أخرى عليهم ويقال لهم : خبرونا عمّن سمعناه يقول : أنا من خلق الشيطان من الذي خلقه؟ فإن قالوا : النور خلقه، قيل لهم : فقد خَلَقَ النُّورِ مَن كَذِبَ، وأضاف خلق نفسِهِ إلى غير خالقِهِ ؛ وإن جاز ذلك جاز أن يخلق الظالم الجائر، وجاز أن يخلق سائر الشرور ، وإن قالوا : الشيطان هو الذي خلق هذا القائل، قيل لهم : فقد صَدَقَ هذا الناطق ؛ فإن جاز أن يخلق الشيطانُ خيراً صادقاً عليه، فما أنكرتم أن يخلق سائر الخير وجميع فاعليه حتى يكون منه الخير والشر؟ وهذا ترك دينكم .
Another objection against them: And it is said to them: inform us about one whom we have heard say: 'I am from the creation of Satan' – who created him? If they say: light created him, it is said to them: then light created one who lied, and attributed the creation of himself to other than his creator; and if that is permissible, then it is permissible that light creates the unjust tyrant, and it is permissible that it creates all other evils. And if they say: Satan created this speaker, it is said to them: then this speaker has told the truth; and if it is permissible that Satan creates good that is truthful about him, why do you deny that he creates all other good and all its doers, so that good and evil both come from him? And this is abandoning your religion.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage contains a dialectical objection (musa'ala) against the dualists who believe in two principles: light (good) and darkness (evil). The author presents a scenario: there is a person who says 'I am from the creation of Satan' – implying he was created by Satan. The dualists are asked: who created this person? Two answers are considered: (1) If they say light created him, then light would have created a liar (since the person falsely claims to be from Satan) and also would have created one who attributes his own creation to someone else (Satan). If light can create such evil, then it could create all evils, contradicting the dualist claim that light only creates good. (2) If they say Satan created him, then the speaker is truthful (since Satan actually created him), meaning Satan created a truthful good act. If Satan can create good, then he could create all good, removing the separation of principles. Either answer leads to contradictions that undermine the dualist religion. The conclusion 'وهذا ترك دينكم' (this is abandoning your religion) indicates the argument forces the dualist to give up their core tenets.

Key Terms
شيطان
نور
خلق
صدق
كذب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection is merely a tricky hypothetical with no real force.
Correction: The objection systematically shows that both possible answers lead to logical contradictions in the dualist worldview, proving its incoherence.

Checkpoint
What is the first possible answer to the question 'Who created the man who says he is from Satan's creation?' that the author presents?
A) The man created himself.
B) Light created him.
C) Darkness created him.
D) God created him.

Key Takeaway
The dualist system cannot coherently explain the existence of a liar who attributes himself to Satan without either making light the source of evil or Satan the source of good.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you catch yourself blaming your mistakes on 'the devil' or on your environment, are you not implicitly adopting a kind of dualism? How does Baqillani's argument force you to take full responsibility for your actions as solely answerable to the One Creator?
?
The person in the example makes a false claim about his origin. Have you ever deceived yourself by attributing your shortcomings to an external source, rather than acknowledging them as your own? What would it mean to stop lying to yourself and accept that good and evil in your life come from the same divine test?
?
If you truly believe that Allah alone creates all things, including your evil deeds, how does that change the way you seek repentance? Are you willing to confront the discomfort that your own choices are part of a divine decree, or do you secretly wish some evils were outside His control so you could blame them elsewhere?

The Apostate's Conversion Unravels Dualism
Baqillani challenges dualists on whether God can create evil, using apostasy as example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqillani uses the case of a converted Magian to refute the dualist belief that good and evil come from separate creators.

Core Idea
One person's conversion forces the dualists to contradict themselves.

Imam Baqillani continues his refutation of the dualists with a concrete example: a Magian who converts to Judaism. This forces the dualists to either admit that God creates evil or deny the obvious reality of personal change. This lesson walks through the logical traps Baqillani sets and shows why the dualist position ultimately collapses.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to grasp the overall dialectical flow.
Notice the repeated pattern: if they say X, then Y follows.
2
Identify the two initial options
Baqillani first asks whether God can create an evil liar. The dualists must answer yes or no. Each answer leads to a trap.
These two branches form the backbone of the objection.
3
Trace the reduction arguments
Trace what happens if they say yes (they abandon their position) and if they say no (the apostate case follows). For the apostate, consider three possible attributions: created by Satan, created by God, or a different person.
Each attribution is shown to be absurd or self-defeating.
4
Reflect on the final absurdity
The dualists' last resort is denying real change in the apostate. Baqillani refutes this by appealing to self-evident experience, making further debate pointless.
This shows the dualist position contradicts necessity and sense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة أخرى عليهم ويقال لهم : هل يجوز أن يخلق الله شريراً كذاباً يعصيه ويشتمه ويفتري عليه؟ فإن قالوا: نعم، تركوا قولهم وقيل لهم : فما أنكرتم أن يكون خالقاً لجميع الشرور؟ وإن قالوا : لا ، قيل لهم : فخبرونا عن رجل كان مجوسياً دائناً بقولكم ثم تهوّدَ وانتقل عن المجوسية وأكفر أهلها، مِن خَلْقٍ مَن هو؟ فإن قالوا من خلقِ الشيطان، قيل : فقد فعل الشيطان خيراً، معتقداً للخير، برهة من الدهر ؛ وإن جاز ذلك جاز أن يخلق جميع الخير؛ وإن قالوا: من خلق الرحمن، قيل لهم : فقد خلق الرحمن الشرير الذي تهود وتزندق وكذب عليه ؛ وإن جاز ذلك جاز أن يفعل سائر الشرور. وإن قالوا : الذي تزندق وتهوّد غير الذي كان مجوسياً، قيل لهم : فعلى هذا ما انتقل أحدٌ قط عن حق اعتقده ؛ والمعتقد للمجوسية على ما هو عليه، وإن صار إلى التدين باليهودية والزندقة، لم يفارق ما اعتقده قط ولا برىء منه وهذا جحد الضرورة والحس لأن الإنسان يجد من نفسه اعتقاداً لغير ما كان معتقداً له وذَمَّه لما كان عليه بعد مدحه له ؛ فلا معنى لمناظرة من انتهى إلى هذا الحد
Another objection against them: And it is said to them: Is it permissible that God creates an evil liar who disobeys Him, reviles Him, and slanders Him? If they say: yes, they abandon their statement, and it is said to them: why then do you deny that He is the creator of all evils? And if they say: no, it is said to them: inform us about a man who was a Magian, adhering to your doctrine, then became a Jew, and transferred from Magianism and declared its people disbelievers – from whose creation is he? If they say: from the creation of Satan, it is said: then Satan has done a good deed, believing in good for a period of time; and if that is permissible, then it is permissible that he creates all good. And if they say: from the creation of the Merciful (i.e., God), it is said to them: then the Merciful has created the evil one who became a Jew and a heretic and lied about Him; and if that is permissible, then He can do all evils. And if they say: the one who became a heretic and a Jew is other than the one who was a Magian, it is said: on this basis, no one has ever transferred from a truth he believed; the one who believed in Magianism remains as he was, and even if he comes to adopt Judaism and heresy, he has never left what he believed nor been free from it – and this is a denial of necessity and sense, because a person finds in himself a belief in something other than what he used to believe and condemns what he was upon after having praised it. So there is no point in arguing with one who has reached this limit.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage presents a second dialectical objection against the dualists. The author first asks whether God can create an evil liar. If the dualists say yes, they abandon their own position that God only creates good. If they say no, the author presents a concrete case: a man who was a Magian (believer in two principles) converts to Judaism and renounces his former religion. The dualists are asked: who created this apostate? Two answers are explored: (1) If they say Satan created him, then Satan has performed a good act by creating this man's belief in Judaism? Actually the argument is more subtle: the apostate 'believed in good' (i'tiqad al-khayr) for a time? Wait, the text says 'فقد فعل الشيطان خيراً، معتقداً للخير' meaning Satan did good, believing in good (i.e., the apostate's act of converting to Judaism might be considered evil by dualists, but the objection turns on the attribution). Actually the text says 'فقد فعل الشيطان خيراً' (Satan did good) – perhaps because the apostate's new belief is considered good? The logic: if Satan created the apostate's conversion, then Satan created a good act (since the conversion is from falsehood to truth? Or simply because the apostate now believes in a different religion). The point is that if Satan can create some good, he can create all good, collapsing dualism. (2) If they say God created him, then God created an evil apostate, so God can create all evil. The dualists might try to escape by saying the apostate is a different person from the original Magian – i.e., no real change. The author refutes this by appealing to self-evident experience: people do change their beliefs, they find themselves believing differently and condemning past beliefs. This reduction ad absurdum shows that the dualist position leads to denying obvious reality, making further debate pointless.

Key Terms
خلق الشرير (creation of the evil one)
تهويد (Judaism)
المجوس (Magians/Zoroastrians)
الانتقال (transfer/conversion)
الضرورة والحس (necessity and sense)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection is about free will vs determinism.
Correction: The objection is specifically aimed at the dualist principle that good and evil come from separate sources. The argument shows the logical impossibility of maintaining such a distinction in face of observable change.

Checkpoint
What is the third possible answer the dualists might give when asked who created the apostate?
A) The apostate created himself.
B) The apostate who became a Jew is a different person from the one who was a Magian.
C) God created him, but he was not originally evil.
D) The apostate's conversion is an illusion.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani shows that change of religion is a self-evident reality that dualists cannot explain without abandoning their core principle.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Baqillani argues that change of belief is self-evident. When was the last time you experienced a genuine shift in your convictions about God or religion? Did you attribute that change to your own effort or to God's guidance? How does this affect your understanding of divine control over all actions, including your own?
?
The dualist denies that a person can truly change, claiming the convert is a different person. In your own life, have you ever treated someone who changed their religion or beliefs as if they were somehow 'not the same person'? What does this lesson reveal about the importance of acknowledging sincere transformation?
?
If God creates both the believer and the apostate, what does that mean for how you view those who have left your faith? Do you see them as a product of God's creation or as purely their own choice? How does this shape your compassion and your prayers for them?

The Origin of Christian Sects and Paul's Deception
Baqillani narrates the origin of Christian sects and the role of Paul in dividing them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's narrative of how Christian sects originated through the deception of Paul, and the key doctrinal corruptions introduced.

Core Idea
Christian divisions trace back to a single scheme of deception by Paul.

In this passage, Baqillani provides a historical account of the fragmentation of Christianity into numerous sects. He traces the origin to a plot by a Jew named Paul who pretended to convert to Christianity in order to corrupt it from within. This narrative serves as a polemical explanation for the divergence of Christian doctrine from the original teachings of Jesus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to grasp the full story. Notice the listing of sects and the dramatic narrative of Paul.
The passage is detailed; take your time.
2
Identify the three main sects
The passage mentions three major groups: Melkites, Nestorians, and Jacobites. Find them in the text and note how they are described.
3
Analyze Paul's role and doctrinal innovations
Paul is the central figure who introduces corrupt teachings: Trinity, divinity and humanity of Jesus, and others. Identify these innovations and how they led to further splits.
Reflect on the polemical nature of this account.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
افترقت النصارى اثنتين وسبعين فرقة وكبار فرقهم ثلاثة : الملكانية، والنسطورية، واليعقوبية، وانشعبت منها الإليانية والبليارسية والمقد انوسية والسبالية والبوطينوسيه، والبولية، إلى سائر الفرق. وكان سبب تفرقهم ما ذكره المفسرون وأصحاب التواريخ وذلك أنهم قالوا: إن النصارى كانوا متمسكين بدين عيسى عليه السلام بعد ما رفع إلى السماء إحدى وثلاثين سنة، وكانوا يجبرون على الاستقامة إلى أن وقع بينهم وبين اليهود حرب . وكان في اليهود رجل اسمه بولس قتل منهم مقتلة عظيمة، ثم قال لليهود إن كان قوم عيسى على الحق ونحن قد كفرنا بهم يكون علينا غبن عظيم فإنهم يدخلون الجنة ونحن ندخل النار، ولكني احتال حيلة حتى أفسد عليهم دينهم، وكان له فرس اسمه عقاب وكان يقاتل عليه . فقام وعقر ذلك الفرس وأظهر الندم على ما كان منه ونثر التراب على رأسه ثم جاء إلى النصارى متندماً بظاهره فقالوا له من أنت؟ فقال: أنا بولس كنت أشد عدو لكم ولكني سمعت من السماء نداء أن توبتك لا تقبل إلا أن تتنصر. الآن تبت ورجعت إلى دينكم فأكرموه وأدخلوه كنيستهم فلازم بيتاً من بيوتها لم يخرج منه ليلا ولا نهاراً حتى تعلم الإنجيل، ثم خرج وقال : سمعت من السماء أن توبتك قد قبلت وأن صدقك قد عرف، وأنك قد أحببت وقبلت . ثم خرج إلى بيت المقدس واستخلف رجلا من نسطور وعلمه أن عیسی ومريم والإله كانوا ثلاثة ثم خرج إلى الروم وعلمهم اللاهوت والناسوت وقال لهم : إن عيسى لم يكن ناساً ثم صار ناساً، ولم يكن جسماً ثم صار جسماً، وكان ابن، وعلم يعقوب هذا القول ثم دعا رجلاً كان اسمه ملكا وقال له : أنت صاحبي خالصاً فإني أريد أن أفضي إليك سر ينبغي أن لا تترك نحلتك هذه وتدعو الخلق إليها فقد رأيت عيسى عليه السلام البارحة في المنام وكان راضياً عني. فينبغي أن لا ترجع عن نحلتك بحال. فإني أريد أن أتقرب إلى الله تعالى بقربان لرضاه عني أذبح نفسي قرباناً . ثم قام ودخل المذبح وزج نفسه . فلما كان اليوم الثالث من وفاته قام كل واحد من أولئك الثلاثة ودعا الناس إلى نحلته . وتبع كل واحد منهم جماعة من الناس وكانوا يتقاتلون فيما بينهم وبقي بينهم ذلك الخلاف . ولم يزالوا يختلفون حتى بلغ عدد فرقهم مثل ما نطق به الخبر المروي في هذا الباب. وكان مذهبهم مذهب أصحاب الهيولى. وكانوا في بعض دينهم مع اليهود، وفي بعضـه مـع النصارى، وابتدعوا من عند أنفسهم أموراً كثيرة تخالف الفريقين.
The Christians split into seventy-two sects, their major groups being three: the Melkites, the Nestorians, and the Jacobites. From them branched the Elyanaeans, the Bilyarsians, the Macedonians, the Sabellians, the Potinoseans, the Paulians, and the rest of the sects. The cause of their division was what the exegetes and historians mentioned: they said that the Christians were adhering to the religion of Jesus, peace be upon him, after he was raised to heaven for thirty-one years, and they were compelled to uprightness until a war occurred between them and the Jews. There was a man among the Jews named Paul who had killed a great number of them. Then he said to the Jews: If the people of Jesus are upon the truth and we have disbelieved in them, we will suffer a great loss, for they will enter Paradise and we will enter the Fire. But I will devise a scheme to corrupt their religion. He had a horse named 'Iqab on which he used to fight. So he stood and hamstrung that horse, and showed remorse for what he had done, and threw dust on his head. Then he came to the Christians with apparent remorse. They said: Who are you? He said: I am Paul, I was your worst enemy, but I heard a call from heaven that your repentance is not accepted unless you become a Christian. Now I have repented and returned to your religion. So they honored him and let him into their church. He stayed in one of its houses, not leaving night or day, until he learned the Gospel. Then he came out and said: I heard from heaven that your repentance has been accepted and your sincerity is known, and that you are loved and accepted. Then he went out to Jerusalem and appointed a man from Nestorius and taught him that Jesus, Mary, and God were three. Then he went out to Rome and taught them the divinity and humanity, and said to them: Jesus was not a human then became a human, and was not a body then became a body, and was a son. And he taught Jacob this statement. Then he called a man named Malika and said to him: You are my sincere companion, I want to confide in you a secret; you should not abandon your sect and should call people to it, for I saw Jesus peace be upon him last night in a dream and he was pleased with me. So you should not turn away from your sect at all. I want to draw near to Allah Almighty by a sacrifice to please Him, I will slaughter myself as a sacrifice. Then he stood and entered the sanctuary and stabbed himself. Then on the third day after his death, each of those three stood and called people to his sect. A group of people followed each of them, and they fought among themselves, and that disagreement remained. They continued to differ until the number of their sects reached what the reported tradition stated in this chapter. Their belief was the belief of the adherents of the matter [hyle]. They were with the Jews in some of their religion, and with the Christians in some of it, and they innovated many things from themselves that opposed both groups.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative about the origin of Christian sects. Baqillani reports that Christians split into seventy-two sects, with three major ones: Melkites, Nestorians, and Jacobites, and many others. The cause was the deception of a Jew named Paul. Paul, after killing many Christians, pretended to repent and infiltrated the Christian community. He learned the Gospel, then claimed divine acceptance. He then taught heretical doctrines: that Jesus, Mary, and God are three (Trinity), and that Jesus had divinity and humanity (lahut and nasut). He influenced Nestorius and a man named Jacob, and later another man named Malika, whom he instructed to maintain his sect. Paul then committed suicide as a supposed sacrifice. After his death, his followers each propagated their own sect, leading to conflict and multiplication of divisions. Their beliefs mixed elements from Jews and Christians, and they innovated many things.

Key Terms
الملكانية
النسطورية
اليعقوبية
بولس
اللاهوت
الناسوت
الهيولى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Baqillani's account of Paul is historically accurate.
Correction: This narrative is a polemical explanation, not necessarily historical fact. It is used to illustrate how Christian doctrine became corrupted.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what was Paul's motive for pretending to convert to Christianity?
A) To gain political power
B) To corrupt their religion from within
C) To become a prophet
D) To seek forgiveness for his sins

Key Takeaway
Baqillani uses the story of Paul to explain the corruption of Christian doctrine and the origin of many sects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Paul appeared outwardly remorseful and zealous, yet his inner intention was corrupt. In your own practice of faith, how do you ensure that your outward acts of worship are matched by sincere intention? Are there any religious habits you perform that you have not examined for sincerity?
?
The Christians initially had a unified religion but were gradually divided by false teachings. Think about your own knowledge of Islam: are there any beliefs or practices you hold that you have not verified against the Quran and authenticated Sunnah? What steps will you take to safeguard yourself from blind following of popular but unverified teachings?
?
Paul used his knowledge of the Gospel to corrupt it from within. This warns us about the misuse of religious knowledge. Have you ever used your knowledge of Islam to argue or manipulate? How can you ensure that your learning brings you closer to humility and service rather than arrogance and division?
