The Origin of the Trinitarian Sect and Its Spread
Baqillani recounts a narrative about the origin of a Christian sect and its division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the narrative account of the origin of a Christian Trinitarian sect as described by Imam Baqillani, including its key doctrines and the events leading to its division.

Core Idea
A narrative reveals how a Trinitarian sect emerged through teachings about Jesus and internal conflict.

Imam Baqillani presents a historical narrative about the beginnings of a Christian Trinitarian sect. This passage describes how a teacher went to Rome, taught the doctrines of divinity and humanity regarding Jesus, and how after a self-sacrifice, the followers split into warring factions. The story illustrates the sect's origins and its doctrinal deviations.

Guided Path
1
Read the narrative carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Pay attention to the sequence of events and the key doctrines mentioned.
Notice that the story begins with a statement about Mary and God being three, which sets the stage for Trinitarian beliefs.
2
Identify the key claims about Jesus
The passage states that Jesus was not a human then became human, and was not a body then became a body. Also, he was called a son. Reflect on these claims.
These claims are foundational to the sect's doctrine.
3
Observe the division and aftermath
Note how after Jacob's self-sacrifice, three individuals each called people to their own sect, leading to conflict and many divisions. Also note the reference to the 'followers of hyle' and the borrowing from Jews and Christians.
This shows how the sect fragmented and adopted various beliefs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومريم والإله كانوا ثلاثة ثم خرج إلى الروم وعلمهم اللاهوت والناسوت وقال لهم: إن عيسى لم يكن ناساً ثم صار ناساً، ولم يكن جسماً ثم صار جسماً، وكان ابن، وعلم يعقوب هذا القول ثم دعا رجلاً كان اسمه ملكا وقال له: أنت صاحبي خالصاً فإني أريد أن أفضي إليك سر ينبغي أن لا تترك نحلتك هذه وتدعو الخلق إليها فقد رأيت عيسى عليه السلام البارحة في المنام وكان راضياً عني. فينبغي أن لا ترجع عن نحلتك بحال. فإني أريد أن أتقرب إلى الله تعالى بقربان لرضاه عني أذبح نفسي قرباناً. ثم قام ودخل المذبح وزج نفسه. فلما كان اليوم الثالث من وفاته قام كل واحد من أولئك الثلاثة ودعا الناس إلى نحلته. وتبع كل واحد منهم جماعة من الناس وكانوا يتقاتلون فيما بينهم وبقي بينهم ذلك الخلاف. ولم يزالوا يختلفون حتى بلغ عدد فرقهم مثل ما نطق به الخبر المروي في هذا الباب. وكان مذهبهم مذهب أصحاب الهيولى. وكانوا في بعض دينهم مع اليهود، وفي بعضـه مـع النصارى، وابتدعوا من عند أنفسهم أموراً كثيرة تخالف الفريقين.
And Mary and God were three, then he went out to Rome and taught them divinity and humanity, and said to them: Indeed, Jesus was not a human then he became a human, and was not a body then he became a body, and he was a son. And Jacob taught this statement, then he called a man whose name was Malka and said to him: You are my pure companion, for I want to confide to you a secret: you should not abandon this sect of yours and call the creation to it, for I saw Jesus, peace be upon him, last night in a dream, and he was pleased with me. So you should not revert from your sect at all. For I want to draw near to God Almighty by a sacrifice for His pleasure: I will sacrifice myself. Then he stood and entered the altar and threw himself. When the third day after his death came, each of those three stood and called the people to his sect. Each one of them was followed by a group of people, and they fought among themselves, and that disagreement remained among them. They continued to differ until the number of their sects reached what the reported tradition in this chapter spoke of. Their doctrine was the doctrine of the followers of hyle. And in some of their religion they were with the Jews, and in some of it with the Christians, and they innovated from themselves many things contradicting the two groups.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage narrates a story about the origin of a Christian Trinitarian sect. It begins by stating that Mary and God were three (i.e., a trinity), then someone (likely a teacher) went to Rome and taught them the doctrine of 'divinity and humanity' (lahut and nasut), claiming that Jesus was not a human then became human, was not a body then became a body, and was a son. Then a person named Jacob taught this statement and called a man named Malka, telling him that he saw Jesus in a dream and Jesus was pleased with him, so Malka should not abandon his sect. Jacob then sacrificed himself. After three days, three individuals each called people to their own sect, leading to conflict and division until many sects formed. Their doctrine is described as that of the 'followers of hyle' (ashab al-hayula), i.e., materialists, and they borrowed from both Jews and Christians while innovating many things contrary to both.

The sect borrowed some beliefs from Jews and some from Christians, yet contradicted both. Consider your own faith: are there areas where you have blended truths with falsehoods, claiming innovation as piety? Ask Allah for guidance to pure truth.

Why Not Four Hypostases? Baqillani's Dialectical Critique
Baqillani critiques the Trinity by questioning why three hypostases and not four.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's dialectical argument against the Christian Trinity, where he shows that accepting the opponents' criteria for three hypostases logically leads to either four or two.

Core Idea
If three, why not four? If power equals life, why not knowledge? Inconsistency exposed.

In this passage, Imam al-Baqillani engages the Christian doctrine of the Trinity using a dialectical method. Instead of outright rejection, he adopts the opponents' framework and presses the logic: if attributes necessitate hypostases, why stop at three? This lesson walks through the exchange, revealing the internal inconsistency of the Trinity claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the flow of the argument come through before you interpret.
Notice the back-and-forth structure: question, answer, counter-question.
2
Identify the initial claim and justification
The opponent claims God is three hypostases: substance, life, and knowledge. Find how they justify this based on God being living and knowing.
The opponent's logic: God is a substance, living, knowing → three hypostases.
3
Trace the author's first counter-argument
Baqillani asks: why not four? Because God is also powerful, requiring a hypostasis of power. See how he extends the opponent's logic.
4
Follow the opponent's attempt to evade
The opponent claims power is identical to life, so only three hypostases. Then Baqillani turns the tables: if power equals life, why not knowledge equals life, reducing to two?
5
Observe the final contradiction
The opponent tries to distinguish knowledge from life based on changeability. Baqillani applies the same reasoning to power, showing power must also be distinct, thus four hypostases. The opponent's position is inconsistent.
The key move: the criterion used to separate knowledge from life also separates power from life.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام عليهم في الأقانيم
يقال لهم : لم زعمتم أن الباري سبحانه ثلاثة أقانيم دون أن تقولوا إنه أربعة وعشرة وأكثر من ذلك؟ فإن قالوا من قبل أنه قد ثبت أن الباري سبحانه موجود جوهر وثبت أنه حي وأنه عالم فوجب أنه واحد ثلاثة أقانيم منها الجوهر الموجود ومنها العلم والحياة جوهر لأن الحي العالم لا يكون حيا عالما حتى يكون ذا حياة وعلم ; فوجب أن الأقانيم ثلاثة ; فيقال لهم : ما أنكرتم من أن تكون الأقانيم أربعة؟ لأننا نقول إن القديم موجود حي عالم قادر ; والقادر لا بد له من قدرة ; فوجب أن تكون الأقانيم أربعة .
فإن قالوا : القدرة هي الحياة، فهما أقنوم واحد ; قيل لهم : فما أنكرتم أن يكون العلم هو الحياة؟ فوجب أن يكون الباري سبحانه أقنومين
فإن قالوا : قد ينقص العلم ويزيد ويوجد ويعدم، والحياة باقية بحالها، فوجب أن يكون العلم ليس من معنى الحياة في شيء; قيل لهم : فكذلك قد تنقص القدرة وتزيد وتعدم جملة، ثم توجد والحياة بحالها ; فوجب أن تكون القدرة غير الحياة وبخلاف معناه .
The discussion against them concerning the hypostases. It is said to them: Why do you claim that the Creator, glorified be He, is three hypostases, rather than saying He is four, ten, or more than that? If they say: Because it is established that the Creator, glorified be He, exists as a substance, and it is established that He is living and that He is knowing, so it necessitates that He is one, three hypostases: the existing substance, and knowledge and life, because the living, knowing being cannot be living and knowing unless he has life and knowledge. So it necessitates that the hypostases are three. It is said to them: Why do you deny that the hypostases are four? Because we say that the Eternal is existing, living, knowing, powerful; and the powerful must have power; so it necessitates that the hypostases are four. If they say: Power is life, so they are one hypostasis. It is said to them: So why do you deny that knowledge is life? Then the Creator, glorified be He, would be two hypostases. If they say: Knowledge may decrease and increase, and exists and ceases, while life remains in its state, so it necessitates that knowledge is not in any way of the meaning of life. It is said to them: Similarly, power may decrease and increase and cease entirely, then exist, while life remains in its state; so it necessitates that power is other than life and contrary to its meaning.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Christian doctrine of the Trinity (أقانيم). The author asks why the opponent claims that God is three hypostases (aqanim) rather than four or more. The opponent replies that it is established that God exists as a substance (جوهر), is living, and is knowing, so He must have three hypostases: substance, life, and knowledge, because a living knowing being must have life and knowledge. The author then asks why not four, adding power, because God is also powerful and power requires a hypostasis. The opponent responds that power is the same as life, so they are one hypostasis. The author retorts: why not say knowledge is the same as life, reducing to two hypostases? The opponent distinguishes by saying that knowledge can increase, decrease, and be absent, while life remains constant, showing knowledge is different from life. The author then turns the argument: similarly, power can increase, decrease, and be absent, so it must be different from life, necessitating four hypostases. The opponent's position is thus shown to be inconsistent.

Key Terms
أقنوم
جوهر
حياة
علم
قدرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This passage is a general rejection of the Trinity without engaging its logic.
Correction: Baqillani uses the opponents' own framework and criteria to show internal inconsistency, not a simple denial.

Checkpoint
What does the author suggest would be the consequence if the opponent argues that knowledge is distinct from life because knowledge can be gained and lost?
A) That power must also be distinct from life
B) That God would have only two hypostases
C) That life and knowledge are the same
D) That the Trinity is proven

Key Takeaway
Baqillani demonstrates that the Christian Trinity is rationally incoherent because the same reasoning that yields three hypostases can be extended to yield four or reduced to two, exposing the opponent's inconsistent application of criteria.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you defend a belief, do you ever find yourself using criteria that you would reject if applied to other parts of your belief system? Where in your life might you be doing this right now, and will you honestly examine it today?
?
Baqillani's method reveals that sometimes we accept claims because they are familiar, not because they are consistent. Is there a belief you hold about God or religion that you have never subjected to the same logical scrutiny you apply to others' beliefs? What would it cost you to test it?
?
The opponent here tried to protect three hypostases by adjusting arguments mid-stream. When your worldview is challenged, do you instinctively patch it with new justifications, or do you allow the challenge to reshape you? Will you pray for the courage to follow truth even if it dismantles your comfort?

Why Not Four Hypostases?
Baqillani questions the number three and argues for four hypostases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the logical critique of the Trinity by adding the attribute of power undermines the Christian justification for three hypostases.

Core Idea
If life and knowledge require hypostases, why not power?

In this passage, Imam al-Baqillani applies a simple but devastating logical test to the Christian doctrine of the Trinity. He notes that if the attributes of life and knowledge each require a separate hypostasis, then consistency demands that power should also have its own. This exposes the arbitrariness of limiting the hypostases to three.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the flow of argument.
2
Identify the Christian position
The opponent argues that God is existent substance, living, and knowing, so three hypostases follow.
Note the terms: جوهر, حي, عالم.
3
Spot the counter-argument
Baqillani adds the attribute of power (قادر) and says power requires a hypostasis, making four.
This exposes inconsistency in the criterion.
4
Consider the implication
If the opponent's method is applied consistently, any attribute could multiply hypostases indefinitely.
This challenges the entire basis for the Trinity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام عليهم في الأقانيم
يقال لهم : لم زعمتم أن الباري سبحانه ثلاثة أقانيم دون أن تقولوا إنه أربعة وعشرة وأكثر من ذلك؟ فإن قالوا من قبل أنه قد ثبت أن الباري سبحانه موجود جوهر وثبت أنه حي وأنه عالم فوجب أنه واحد ثلاثة أقانيم منها الجوهر الموجود ومنها العلم والحياة جوهر لأن الحيَّ العالم لا يكون حيّاً عالماً حتى يكون ذا حياة وعلم ; فوجب أن الأقانيم ثلاثة ; فيقال لهم : ما أنكرتم من أن تكون الأقانيم أربعة? لأننا نقول إن القديم موجود حي عالم قادر ; والقادر لا بدّ له من قدرة ; فوجب أن تكون الأقانيم أربعة .
The discourse against them concerning the hypostases. It is said to them: Why do you claim that the Creator, exalted is He, is three hypostases, and you do not say that He is four, ten, and more than that? If they say: Because it has been established that the Creator, exalted is He, is an existent substance, and it has been established that He is living and that He is knowing, so it is necessary that He is one [in] three hypostases: from them the existent substance, and from them knowledge and life—a substance—because the living, knowing [being] is not living, knowing until he possesses life and knowledge; so it is necessary that the hypostases are three. Then it is said to them: What prevents you from [saying] that the hypostases are four? Because we say that the Eternal is existent, living, knowing, powerful; and the powerful must have power; so it is necessary that the hypostases are four.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is the opening of a refutation of the Christian doctrine of the hypostases (الأقانيم). The author first states the Christian claim that God is three hypostases and immediately challenges why they stop at three, asking why not four, ten, or more. The opponent responds by grounding the three in the attributes of existence, life, and knowledge, arguing that these three attributes require distinct hypostases. The author then counters by adding power (قدرة) to the list of divine attributes, concluding that if the same reasoning is applied, power would demand a fourth hypostasis. This sets up the core logical problem: the criterion for what makes an attribute a hypostasis is arbitrary.

Key Takeaway
The Christian criterion for identifying hypostases is arbitrary, as demonstrated by adding the attribute of power.

?

Reducing Hypostases by Reductio
Baqillani reduces the hypostases to two by questioning the distinction of knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses a reductio ad absurdum to expose inconsistency in the opponent's identification of divine attributes.

Core Idea
One reduction leads to another: if power equals life, why not knowledge too?

In this brief dialectical exchange, Baqillani anticipates an objection from his opponents who attempt to reduce the number of divine hypostases by identifying power with life. Rather than rejecting their move outright, he cleverly turns their own logic against them, showing that if one attribute can be reduced to life, then so can another—leading to an even smaller number of hypostases than they intended. This lesson unpacks the rhetorical and logical strategy behind this argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the literal translation. Notice the compact style and the structure: opponent's claim followed by the author's counter.
The Arabic uses 'فإن قالوا... قيل لهم' a typical dialectical formula.
2
Identify the logical move
The opponent claims power is life, making one hypostasis. The author responds: why not also say knowledge is life? This applies the same logic to another attribute, leading to a different conclusion (two hypostases). Recognize that this is a reductio ad absurdum: the opponent's principle (identifying attributes) leads to an unwanted outcome.
The author does not accept the identification; he uses it against them.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: Why is this argument effective? It shows that if the opponent's method of identification is allowed, it can be extended arbitrarily, contradicting their own position. This demonstrates the inconsistency in selectively identifying only some attributes.
This illustrates a key kalam method: showing that an opponent's premise leads to absurdity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : القدرة هي الحياة، فهما أقنوم واحد ; قيل لهم : فما أنكرتم أن يكون العلم هو الحياة? فوجب أن يكون الباري سبحانه أقنومين
If they say: 'Power is life, so they are one hypostasis,' it is said to them: 'Then what prevents you from [saying] that knowledge is life? So it is necessary that the Creator, exalted is He, [be] two hypostases.'
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is a quick dialectical exchange. The opponent, faced with the argument for four hypostases, tries to reduce the count by identifying power with life, claiming they are one hypostasis. The author immediately turns this against them: if power can be reduced to life, why not also reduce knowledge to life? If both are the same, then only two hypostases remain (substance and life). This shows the inconsistency in the opponent's attempt to selectively identify attributes.

Key Terms
القدرة
الحياة
العلم
أقنوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This passage shows that Baqillani believes there are only two hypostases.
Correction: The passage is a reductio ad absurdum; Baqillani does not endorse the two-hypostasis view. He is showing that the opponent's logic leads to an absurdity, not advocating it himself.

Checkpoint
How does the author respond to the claim that power is the same as life?
A) He agrees and says there are two hypostases total.
B) He asks why knowledge cannot also be identified with life, leading to two hypostases.
C) He argues that power is distinct from life based on scripture.
D) He changes the subject to other attributes.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani uses a reductio ad absurdum to show that arbitrarily identifying attributes leads to unacceptable consequences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were the opponent in this debate and Baqillani turned your own argument against you, how would that feel? What does this teach you about the danger of making arbitrary assumptions in theology?
?
This lesson shows a logical reductio that forces consistency. Reflect on your own beliefs: is there any position you hold that, if applied consistently, would lead to a conclusion you reject? What would it take for you to re-examine that position?
?
Baqillani's argument reveals that accepting one identification of attributes leads to a chain reaction. In your own study of Islamic theology, are you careful to check that your understanding of divine attributes is internally consistent, or do you sometimes accept pieces of different systems without testing their coherence?

Arguments from Variability and Absence of Power
Baqillani uses the variability and absence of power to distinguish it from life.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the variability and occasional absence of power (while life persists) to demonstrate that power is a distinct attribute from life.

Core Idea
What can come and go cannot be the same as what always stays.

In this passage, Baqillani responds to Christian theologians who argued that because knowledge can increase, decrease, and even vanish (as in sleep), it cannot be identical to life. He cleverly turns their own reasoning against them: power also fluctuates and can be entirely absent during paralysis, while life remains. This proves that power is also distinct from life—a key step in establishing the four divine attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument from variation
Read the first part where the opponent's claim about knowledge is presented, and then Baqillani's parallel application to power.
Notice the structure: 'If they say... it is said to them...'
2
Read the argument from absence
Read the second part where the opponent uses sleep/fainting, and Baqillani responds with paralysis.
The pattern is identical: the opponent's own method is used against them.
3
Identify the conclusion
Find the phrase 'فوجب أن تكون القدرة غير الحياة وأن الأقانيم أربعة'. This is the conclusion: power is other than life, and the hypostases are four.
The hypostases refer to the Christian Trinity plus one? Actually, in context, Baqillani is arguing that if knowledge and power are separate, then there are four distinct attributes.
4
Reflect on the rhetorical strategy
Consider why Baqillani uses the opponent's own argument. What does this achieve?
It strengthens the case by using accepted premises.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : قد ينقص العلم ويزيد ويوجد ويعدم، والحياة باقية بحالها، فوجب أن يكون العلم ليس من معنى الحياة في شيء; قيل لهم : فكذلك قد تنقص القدرة وتزيد وتعدم جملة، ثم توجد والحياة بحالها ; فوجب أن تكون القدرة غير الحياة وبخلاف معناه .
فإن قالوا قد يبطل العلم جملة في حالة النوم والغشي والإنسان حي ; قيل لهم : وكذلك قد تبطل القدرة جملة حتى لا يقدر الإنسان على تحريك يده أو لسانه أو إيماء بعض جوارحه، وهو حي في تلك الحال فوجب أن تكون القدرة غير الحياة وأن الأقانيم أربعة . فإن قالوا : دخول حرف المبالغة في صفة العالم في قولنا عالم وأعلم منه واستحالة المبالغة في صفة الحيّ والتفضيل بين الحيين دليل على أن العلم ليس من الحياة في شيء، قيل لهم : فقولوا لأجل هذا بعينه : إن القدرة غير الحياة لأننا قد نبالغ في صفة القادر ونقول: قادر وأقدر منه، ولا نقول : حي وأحيا منه ; فوجب أن تكون القدرة غير الحياة.
If they say: 'Knowledge may decrease and increase, exist and cease to exist, while life remains in its state, so it is necessary that knowledge is not at all from the meaning of life,' it is said to them: 'Likewise, power may decrease and increase and cease to exist entirely, then exist while life remains in its state; so it is necessary that power is other than life and contrary to its meaning.' If they say: 'Knowledge may entirely cease in the state of sleep and fainting while the human is alive,' it is said to them: 'Likewise, power may entirely cease so that the human cannot move his hand or tongue or gesture with some of his limbs, while he is alive in that state, so it is necessary that power is other than life and that the hypostases are four.' If they say: 'The entry of the letter of exaggeration in the attribute of the knowing in our saying 'knowing' and 'more knowing than him' and the impossibility of exaggeration in the attribute of the living and the comparison between the living indicate that knowledge is not at all from life,' it is said to them: 'Then say for this very reason that power is other than life, because we may exaggerate in the attribute of the powerful and say 'powerful' and 'more powerful than him,' and we do not say 'living' and 'more living than him'; so it is necessary that power is other than life.'
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage presents three distinct arguments to prove that power (قدرة) is a distinct attribute from life (حياة), and by extension that the hypostases should be four. First argument: knowledge can increase and decrease, and can be absent while life persists; the opponent uses this to show knowledge is not life. The author turns the argument around: power also increases and decreases and can cease entirely while life remains, so power is not life either. Second argument: knowledge can be absent during sleep or fainting while the person is still alive; similarly, power can be absent (e.g., paralysis) while the person is alive. Third argument: the comparative and superlative forms (المبالغة) are used for 'knowing' (عالم وأعلم) and for 'powerful' (قادر وأقدر) but not for 'living' (no one says أحيا), indicating that knowledge and power share a feature that life lacks, so they are distinct. Each argument concludes that power is other than life, and thus the hypostases are four.

Misconception: Some might think that if power can be absent while life is present, then power is a temporary attribute that God does not have.
Correction: Baqillani is not denying that God has power; he is arguing that power is a distinct attribute from life, but both are eternal and necessary in God.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani demonstrates that power is a distinct attribute from life by showing that power can vary and be absent while life remains constant.

The Superlative Forms Argument
Baqillani uses the absence of superlative for 'living' to prove power is distinct.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the existence of superlative forms for 'knowing' and 'powerful' but not for 'living' to argue that power and knowledge are distinct from life.

Core Idea
If life were the source of power, we could say 'more living,' but we don't.

The opponents try to use a linguistic argument: because we can say 'more knowing' (أعلم) but not 'more living' (أحيا), knowledge must be something additional to life. Baqillani applies the same logic to power: we can say 'more powerful' (أقدر) but not 'more living,' so power too is distinct from life. This linguistic observation reinforces the previous arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's linguistic argument
The opponent claims that the ability to form a superlative for 'knowing' but not for 'living' shows knowledge is not life.
This is a subtle argument based on Arabic usage.
2
See Baqillani's response
Baqillani says: apply the same reasoning to power. We say 'more powerful' but not 'more living.' Thus power is not life either.
The structure is again: if they say... it is said to them...
3
Understand the linguistic point
The superlative form (المبالغة) indicates that the attribute can be intensified, which is not the case for life.
In theology, life is an essential attribute that does not admit of degrees.
4
Connect to the conclusion
The conclusion is the same: power is other than life.
This third argument reinforces the earlier ones.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : قد ينقص العلم ويزيد ويوجد ويعدم، والحياة باقية بحالها، فوجب أن يكون العلم ليس من معنى الحياة في شيء; قيل لهم : فكذلك قد تنقص القدرة وتزيد وتعدم جملة، ثم توجد والحياة بحالها ; فوجب أن تكون القدرة غير الحياة وبخلاف معناه .
فإن قالوا قد يبطل العلم جملة في حالة النوم والغشي والإنسان حي ; قيل لهم : وكذلك قد تبطل القدرة جملة حتى لا يقدر الإنسان على تحريك يده أو لسانه أو إيماء بعض جوارحه، وهو حي في تلك الحال فوجب أن تكون القدرة غير الحياة وأن الأقانيم أربعة . فإن قالوا : دخول حرف المبالغة في صفة العالم في قولنا عالم وأعلم منه واستحالة المبالغة في صفة الحيّ والتفضيل بين الحيين دليل على أن العلم ليس من الحياة في شيء، قيل لهم : فقولوا لأجل هذا بعينه : إن القدرة غير الحياة لأننا قد نبالغ في صفة القادر ونقول: قادر وأقدر منه، ولا نقول : حي وأحيا منه ; فوجب أن تكون القدرة غير الحياة.
If they say: 'Knowledge may decrease and increase, exist and cease to exist, while life remains in its state, so it is necessary that knowledge is not at all from the meaning of life,' it is said to them: 'Likewise, power may decrease and increase and cease to exist entirely, then exist while life remains in its state; so it is necessary that power is other than life and contrary to its meaning.' If they say: 'Knowledge may entirely cease in the state of sleep and fainting while the human is alive,' it is said to them: 'Likewise, power may entirely cease so that the human cannot move his hand or tongue or gesture with some of his limbs, while he is alive in that state, so it is necessary that power is other than life and that the hypostases are four.' If they say: 'The entry of the letter of exaggeration in the attribute of the knowing in our saying 'knowing' and 'more knowing than him' and the impossibility of exaggeration in the attribute of the living and the comparison between the living indicate that knowledge is not at all from life,' it is said to them: 'Then say for this very reason that power is other than life, because we may exaggerate in the attribute of the powerful and say 'powerful' and 'more powerful than him,' and we do not say 'living' and 'more living than him'; so it is necessary that power is other than life.'
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage presents three distinct arguments to prove that power (قدرة) is a distinct attribute from life (حياة), and by extension that the hypostases should be four. First argument: knowledge can increase and decrease, and can be absent while life persists; the opponent uses this to show knowledge is not life. The author turns the argument around: power also increases and decreases and can cease entirely while life remains, so power is not life either. Second argument: knowledge can be absent during sleep or fainting while the person is still alive; similarly, power can be absent (e.g., paralysis) while the person is alive. Third argument: the comparative and superlative forms (المبالغة) are used for 'knowing' (عالم وأعلم) and for 'powerful' (قادر وأقدر) but not for 'living' (no one says أحيا), indicating that knowledge and power share a feature that life lacks, so they are distinct. Each argument concludes that power is other than life, and thus the hypostases are four.

Extension to More Attributes
Baqillani extends the argument to will, remaining, hearing, seeing, and speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani extends the argument for hypostases to additional divine attributes and refutes Christian objections.

Core Idea
The logic of hypostases leads to absurd multiplication if applied consistently.

Imam Baqillani continues his debate with Christians by extending the same logical pattern to more divine attributes. He shows that if the opponent insists on deducing hypostases from attributes, there is no stopping at three—the same reasoning would yield many more. The passage then addresses several objections the opponent might raise, turning their own logic against them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the new attributes
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. List the five additional attributes Baqillani introduces beyond the initial three.
The attributes are will, remaining, hearing, seeing, and speech.
2
Trace the argument pattern
Notice how Baqillani repeats the same reasoning: each attribute necessitates a distinct hypostasis. This reveals the opponent's inconsistency.
3
Analyze the objections and responses
Examine each objection the opponent might raise and how Baqillani turns it back on them, showing that their own principles lead to more hypostases or to absurdity.
The passage ends mid-sentence; the conclusion is missing.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك يقال لهم : ما أنكرتم أن تكون الأقانيم خمسة وعشرة? لأننا نقول : إن الباري موجود حي عالم قادر ; ونقول: إنه مريد وباق وسميع وبصير ومتكلم ; والباقي السميع البصير المتكلم المريد لا يكون كذلك إلا لوجود بقاء وإرادة وسمع وبصر وكلام . فإن قالوا البقاء هو هو، قيل لهم : والحياة والعلم هما هو? فقولوا إنه أقنوم واحد. فإن قالوا : الكلام والإرادة فعل من أفعال المتكلم المريد، قيل لهم : وكذلك العلم فعل من أفعال العالم ; فقولوا : إنه أقنومان. فإن قالوا : قد يعلم بالعلم من لم يفعله، قيل لهم : وقد يريد بالإرادة ويتكلم بالكلام من لا يفعله ; وكذلك إن قالوا سمع الباري سبحانه وبصره هو نفس علمه فوجب أنهما ليس
And likewise it is said to them: 'What prevents you from [saying] that the hypostases are five and ten? Because we say that the Creator is existent, living, knowing, powerful; and we say: He is willing, remaining, hearing, seeing, and speaking; and the remaining, the hearing, the seeing, the speaking, the willing are not so except by the existence of remaining, will, hearing, sight, and speech.' If they say: 'Remaining is identical [to something],' it is said to them: 'Are life and knowledge identical? Then say that He is one hypostasis.' If they say: 'Speech and will are an act of the speaker and willer,' it is said to them: 'Likewise, knowledge is an act of the knower; then say that there are two hypostases.' If they say: 'One may know by knowledge without [himself] performing it,' it is said to them: 'And one may will by will and speak by speech without performing it.' And likewise, if they say: 'The hearing and sight of the Creator, exalted is He, are the same as His knowledge,' so it is necessary that they are not...
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
In this passage, the author extends the argument to additional divine attributes: will (إرادة), remaining/eternity (بقاء), hearing (سمع), seeing (بصر), and speech (كلام). He asks why the hypostases are not five or ten, since each of these attributes, following the same logic, would require a distinct hypostasis. The author then anticipates and refutes possible objections: (1) If the opponent says 'remaining is identical (to something else),' the author retorts: 'Then are life and knowledge identical? If so, you should say one hypostasis.' (2) If the opponent says 'speech and will are acts of the agent,' the author points out that knowledge could also be considered an act, leading to two hypostases. (3) If the opponent says 'one may know by knowledge without performing it,' the author notes the same applies to will and speech. The passage ends abruptly while addressing the claim that hearing and sight are the same as knowledge.

The Argument from Nullification of Knowledge and Power in Sleep
Baqillani argues that nullification of power in sleep proves power is distinct from life.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the nullification of power in sleep to argue that power is distinct from life, and how this refutes the Christian claim of three hypostases.

Core Idea
Power's absence in sleep proves it is distinct from life — making four hypostases.

In this passage, Baqillani responds to a trinitarian objection that knowledge can be absent in sleep while life remains. He turns the argument around: power is also absent in sleep, yet life remains, so power must be distinct from life. This leads to the conclusion that there are at least four hypostases (essence, life, knowledge, power), not three. Understanding this argument helps clarify the Islamic critique of Christian theological categories.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the first part: the claim that knowledge is nullified in sleep while life remains. Note that this is the opponent's starting point.
2
Find Baqillani's reply
Read the second part: he applies the same logic to power, which is also nullified in sleep. Understand that the parallel forces the opponent to accept that power is distinct from life.
3
Draw the conclusion
Connect the dots: if knowledge and power are both distinct from life, then the hypostases are at least four (essence, life, knowledge, power). This undercuts the Christian claim of three.
4
Reflect on the argument's strength
Ask: why does this work? Because the opponent's own reasoning (nullification indicates distinction) is applied consistently. This shows the power of logical consistency in theological debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا قد يبطل العلم جملة في حالة النوم والغشي والإنسان حي؛ قيل لهم: وكذلك قد تبطل القدرة جملة حتى الإنسان لا يقدر على تحريك يده أو لسانه أو إيماء بعض جوارحه، وهو حي في تلك الحال فوجب أن تكون القدرة غير الحياة وأن الأقانيم أربعة.
If they say: knowledge is completely nullified in the state of sleep and fainting, while the human is alive; it is said to them: likewise power is completely nullified, such that the human is unable to move his hand or tongue or to gesture with some of his limbs, while he is alive in that state; so it is necessary that power is other than life, and that the hypostases are four.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer argument against the Christian trinitarian doctrine. The objection claims that knowledge is sometimes nullified (e.g., in sleep or fainting) even though a person remains alive, implying knowledge is distinct from life. The answer uses the same logic: power is also nullified in such states (the person cannot move), yet remains alive; therefore power is distinct from life. If life, knowledge, and power are each distinct, then there must be at least four hypostases (life, knowledge, power, and essence), contradicting the claim of three hypostases.

أقنوم

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think this argument disproves that God has knowledge or power, or that it denies the unity of divine attributes.
Correction: Baqillani is not denying divine attributes; he is using a human example to test the internal consistency of the Christian hypostasis model. The argument only shows that if the opponent's reasoning is applied consistently, it leads to four hypostases, not three.

Checkpoint

C) Sleep proves that humans are not alive.
D) The hypostases are five.

Key Takeaway
In sleep, power is nullified while life persists, proving power is distinct from life — a point that refutes the trinitarian claim of three hypostases.

Elative Forms and Divine Attribute Distinction
Baqillani uses comparative adjectives to prove power is distinct from life.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses Arabic grammatical elative forms to distinguish divine attributes like power from life.

Core Idea
Elative forms reveal essential attribute distinctions.

Baqillani continues his debate with Christian trinitarians by turning their own linguistic argument against them. The Christians argued that because we can say 'more knowledgeable' but not 'more living', knowledge is distinct from life. Baqillani responds that the same logic proves power is also distinct from life, further undermining their doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the first part of the passage where the Christian opponents present their argument using elative forms for knowledge and life.
Notice they claim the elative shows knowledge is not from life.
2
Identify the linguistic claim
Focus on the phrases 'عالم وأعلم منه' vs 'حي وأحيا منه' to see how Arabic grammar treats these attributes differently.
The elative form is possible for 'knowing' but not for 'living'.
3
Read Baqillani's answer
Read the second part where Baqillani turns the argument back: the same logic applies to power ('قادر وأقدر منه').
4
See the reasoning
Understand that the same linguistic pattern (elative possible for power, not for life) forces the conclusion that power is distinct from life.
Baqillani uses their own method against them.
5
Understand the theological implication
Reflect on how this argument undermines the Christian doctrine of the trinity by increasing the number of distinct attributes.
The logic would force an infinite regress of distinct attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: دخول حرف المبالغة في صفة العالم في قولنا عالم وأعلم منه واستحالة المبالغة في صفة الحيّ والتفضيل بين الحيين دليل على أن العلم ليس من الحياة في شيء، قيل لهم: فقولوا لأجل هذا بعينه: إن القدرة غير الحياة لأننا قد نبالغ في صفة القادر ونقول: قادر وأقدر منه، ولا نقول: حي وأحيا منه؛ فوجب أن تكون القدرة غير الحياة.
If they say: the entry of the intensive particle in the description of the knower in our saying 'knowing' and 'more knowing than him' and the impossibility of intensiveness in the description of the living and preference between the living is evidence that knowledge is not from life at all, it is said to them: then say for precisely this same reason that power is other than life, because we may use intensiveness in the description of the powerful and say 'powerful' and 'more powerful than him', and we do not say 'living' and 'more living than him'; so it is necessary that power is other than life.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage continues the refutation of the trinity with another objection-and-answer. The objection notes that in Arabic, we can use the elative form ('af'al') for the attribute of knowledge (we say 'more knowledgeable') but not for life (we do not say 'more living'). This shows knowledge is not identical to life. The answer turns the argument back: the same reasoning applies to power (we say 'more powerful' but not 'more living'), so power must also be distinct from life. This again increases the number of hypostases.

Key Terms
المبالغة
عالم
قادر
حي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument is purely theological and not linguistic.
Correction: Baqillani's argument relies on Arabic grammatical patterns (elative forms) to derive ontological conclusions about divine attributes.

D) Power is always present in life.

Key Takeaway
The inability to use elative forms for a supposed attribute indicates that attribute is not separable from the essence.

The Multiplicity of Hypostases Beyond Three
Baqillani shows that accepting distinct attributes leads to more than three hypostases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses a series of conditional arguments to show that the Christian doctrine of three hypostases leads to an absurd multiplicity.

Core Idea
Accepting distinct attributes as hypostases leads to an indefinite number, not just three.

Baqillani now turns the Christians' own reasoning against them. If attributes like life, knowledge, will, etc. are distinct hypostases, then why stop at three? By applying their logic consistently, Baqillani forces the opponent into absurd conclusions. This passage is a masterclass in reductio ad absurdum within theological debate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to grasp the flow. Then read the translation. Notice how Baqillani presents a series of conditional arguments.
The passage is short but dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the logical moves
The passage contains four distinct conditional objections. Try to list them: (1) If endurance is identical to essence, then life and knowledge also are; (2) If will and speech are acts, then knowledge is also an act; (3) If knowing without acting is allowed, then willing and speaking without acting is also allowed; (4) If hearing and sight are identical to knowledge, then knowledge is identical to life.
Each move is a 'if...then' that mirrors the Christian's own claims.
3
Understand the goal of each move
Each move aims to show that the Christians cannot consistently hold to three hypostases. The first move reduces to one, the second to two, the third allows many, and the fourth again leads to two.
The overall conclusion: no answer from the Christians.
4
Reflect on the method
Baqillani is using the principle of 'what applies to one applies to all' (qiyas). He takes a Christian statement and applies the same logic elsewhere to show inconsistency.
This is a common dialectical technique in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك يقال لهم: ما أنكرتم أن تكون الأقانيم خمسة وعشرة؟ لأننا نقول: إن الباري موجود حي عالم قادر؛ ونقول: إنه مريد وباق وسميع وبصير ومتكلم؛ والباقي السميع البصير المتكلم المريد لا يكون كذلك إلا لوجود بقاء وإرادة وسمع وبصر وكلام. فإن قالوا البقاء هو هو، قيل لهم: والحياة والعلم هما هو؟ فقولوا إنه أقنوم واحد. فإن قالوا: الكلام والإرادة فعل من أفعال المتكلم المريد، قيل لهم: وكذلك العلم فعل من أفعال العالم؛ فقولوا: إنه أقنومان. فإن قالوا: قد يعلم بالعلم من لم يفعله، قيل لهم: وقد يريد بالإرادة ويتكلم بالكلام من لا يفعله؛ وكذلك إن قالوا سمع الباري وبصره هو نفس علمه فوجب أنهما ليسا باقنومين غير العلم قيل لهم: وكذلك علم الباري هو حياته فوجب أن يكون أقنومين؛ ولا جواب لهم عن شيء من ذلك.
And likewise it is said to them: what prevents you from saying the hypostases are five and ten? Because we say: the Creator is existent, living, knowing, powerful; and we say: He is willing, enduring, hearing, seeing, speaking; and the enduring, hearing, seeing, speaking, willing is not so except by the existence of endurance, will, hearing, sight, and speech. If they say endurance is identical [to essence], it is said to them: and life and knowledge are also identical? Then say it is one hypostasis. If they say speech and will are acts of the speaker and willer, it is said to them: likewise knowledge is an act of the knower; then say there are two hypostases. If they say one may know by knowledge without having performed it, it is said to them: and one may will by will and speak by speech without having performed it; and likewise if they say God's hearing and sight are identical to His knowledge, so they are necessarily not two hypostases other than knowledge, it is said to them: and likewise God's knowledge is His life, so it must be that they are two hypostases; and there is no answer for them concerning any of that.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is a multi-step refutation showing that the Christian logic leads to an indefinite number of hypostases. Baqillani lists attributes: existence, life, knowledge, power, will, endurance, hearing, sight, speech. If the Christian claims that some attributes (like endurance) are identical to the essence, then the same should apply to life and knowledge, reducing to one hypostasis. If they claim will and speech are acts, then knowledge should also be an act, giving two hypostases. If they claim one can possess knowledge without having acted, then the same applies to will and speech. Finally, if they claim hearing and sight are identical to knowledge, then similarly knowledge is identical to life, leading to two hypostases. The argument traps the opponent in inconsistency, concluding they have no valid response.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Baqillani is asserting that God has many distinct hypostases.
Correction: He is using the Christians' own reasoning to show it leads to absurd conclusions; he does not affirm multiple hypostases.

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani argue would happen if Christians claim that will and speech are acts?
A) Then knowledge would also be an act, leading to two hypostases.
B) Then there would be five hypostases.
C) Then God would not be omnipotent.
D) Then life and knowledge would be identical.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani demonstrates that the Christian logic of distinct attributes leads to an indefinite multiplicity of hypostases, thus undermining the doctrine of three.

Are you willing to abandon a cherished idea if it fails the test of logical consistency, even if that idea is comforting? What specific idea will you put to the test this week?

Refuting the Christian Limitation of Hypostases
Baqillani refutes the Christian claim that hypostases are only for self-referential attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqillani refutes the Christian claim that hypostases are limited to self-referential attributes, showing it leads to an infinite number of hypostases and undermines the trinity.

Core Idea
If self-referential attributes define hypostases, then many more than three arise, breaking the trinity.

This passage presents a Christian counter-argument that hypostases only apply to attributes that relate to God Himself, such as existence, substance, life, and knowledge. Baqillani turns this logic against them, showing that other self-referential attributes like being eternal or enduring would also qualify, multiplying hypostases beyond three. This effectively refutes the Trinity.

Guided Path
1
Read the Christian claim
Read the first part where the Christian speaker defines hypostasis as only for self-referential attributes (existence, substance, life, knowledge). Note that they use these to justify exactly three hypostases.
2
Follow Baqillani's counter
Baqillani adds attributes like being eternal and being enduring, which are also self-referential. He asks: if these are hypostases too, then there would be more than three.
3
Understand the logical conclusion
The Christian position collapses because they cannot limit the number of self-referential attributes. Baqillani concludes that this argument abandons the trinity.
4
Reflect on the method
Notice Baqillani's dialectical method: he accepts the Christian definition but shows it leads to absurdity, thus refuting them without relying on Islamic premises.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال منهم قائل: الأقنومية إنما تثبت للباري بصفة إلى نفسه لا تعلق لها بغيره وهي كونه موجوداً وجوهراً يرجع إلى نفسه وكونه حيا يرجع إليه ولا تعلق له بغيره وكونه عالماً بنفسه صفة يرجع بها إلى نفسه وإنما له أقنوم بكونه عالماً بنفسه لا بغيره؛ قيل لهم: وكذلك هو قديم بنفسه وليس كل موجود جوهراً قديماً بنفسه؟ فوجب أن يكون كونه قديماً أقنوماً رابعاً؛ وكذلك كونه باقياً صفة هو شيء موجود بنفسه وجوهر بنفسه فيجب أن يكون كونه شيئاً موجوداً أقنوماً وكونه جوهراً أقنوماً لأنه ليس كل موجود جوهراً يرجع إلى نفسه لا تعلق له بغيره، وليس كل موجود باقياً، فيجب أن يكون كونه باقياً أقنوماً خامساً، ولا جواب لهم عن ذلك، وفيه ترك التثليث.
If a speaker among them says: hypostasis is only established for the Creator by an attribute relating to Himself, having no relation to other than Him, and it is His being existent and a substance referring to Himself, and His being living referring to Him, having no relation to other than Him, and His being knowing by Himself, an attribute by which He refers to Himself, and He only has a hypostasis by His being knowing by Himself, not by other than Him; it is said to them: and likewise He is eternal by Himself, and is every existent a substance eternal by Himself? So it must be that His being eternal is a fourth hypostasis; and likewise His being enduring is an attribute, He is something existent by Himself and a substance by Himself, so it must be that His being a thing existent is a hypostasis and His being a substance is a hypostasis, because not every existent is a substance referring to Himself, having no relation to other than Him, and not every existent is enduring, so it must be that His being enduring is a fifth hypostasis, and there is no answer for them concerning that, and in it is the abandonment of the trinity.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage presents a Christian counter-argument and its refutation. The Christian claims that hypostasis (aqnūm) is only applied to attributes that are self-referential (relating to God's essence, not to creation) such as existence, substance, life, and knowledge. Baqillani turns this against them: being eternal by Himself is also a self-referential attribute, so it should be a fourth hypostasis. Similarly, being a substance, being a thing, being enduring are all self-referential, adding a fifth, sixth, etc. This shows the arbitrary limitation to three hypostases is unsustainable. The final phrase 'and in it is the abandonment of the trinity' means the Christian position is refuted, effectively abandoning the trinity.

Misconception: Baqillani is affirming multiple hypostases in God.
Correction: Baqillani is not affirming that; he is using the Christian's own definition to show that it logically leads to many hypostases, which undermines their claim of exactly three.

A) That there are exactly three hypostases.
B) That being eternal by itself would be a fourth hypostasis.
C) That only knowledge is a hypostasis.
D) That life is not a hypostasis.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes the Christian limitation of hypostases by showing that the same logic would produce many hypostases, thereby abandoning the trinity.

The Argument Against Three Hypostases
Baqillani refutes the Christian hypostasis doctrine by reductio ad absurdum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqillani refutes the Christian doctrine of three hypostases by demonstrating that the logic used to define them actually requires more than three, thereby abandoning the Trinity.

Core Idea
Christian hypostatic logic leads to more than three hypostases, not three.

In this passage, Imam Baqillani confronts the Christian claim that God has three hypostases (aqānīm) based on attributes like knowledge and life. He first presents their reasoning, then turns it against them by demonstrating that the same logic would require additional hypostases such as eternity and everlastingness. The result is an absurd multiplication that abandons the Trinity.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Christian Claim
Read the Christian argument: hypostases are attributes that refer only to God's essence, such as being existent, substance, living, and knowledgeable. They claim God has a hypostasis for being knowledgeable by Himself.
This is the position Baqillani will refute.
2
Identify the Initial Comparison
Baqillani points out that if knowledge and life are both hypostases, then since God's knowledge is His life, the Christian would have to say God has two hypostases for these two attributes, but they already claim three total.
3
Follow the Refutation
Now apply the same criterion to other attributes: God is eternal by Himself, everlasting, a thing, and a substance. Each of these also refers only to His essence, so they would each be a separate hypostasis.
This shows the logic leads to at least five hypostases.
4
Realize the Conclusion
Since the Christian definition leads to more than three hypostases, the doctrine of the Trinity is abandoned. The argument is a reductio ad absurdum.
Baqillani concludes that they have no answer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باقنومين غير العلم قيل لهم : وكذلك علم الباري سبحانه هو حياته فوجب أن يكون أقنومين ؛ ولا جواب لهم عن شيء من ذلك . فإن قال منهم قائل : الأقنومية إنما تثبت للباري بصفة إلى نفسه لا تعلق لها بغيره وهي كونه موجوداً وجوهراً يرجع إلى نفسه وكونه حيا يرجع إليه ولا تعلق له بغيره وكونه عالماً بنفسه صفة يرجع بها إلى نفسه ؛ وإنما له أقنوم بكونه عالماً بنفسه لا بغيره ؛ قيل لهم : وكذلك هو قديم بنفسه وليس كل موجود جوهراً قديماً بنفسه؟ فوجب أن يكون كونه قديماً أقنوماً رابعاً ؛ وكذلك كونه باقياً صفة هو . هو شيء موجود بنفسه وجوهر بنفسه فيجب أن يكون كونه شيئاً موجوداً أقنوماً وكونه جوهراً أقنوماً لأنه ليس كل موجود جوهراً يرجع إلى نفسه لا تعلق له بغيره، وليس كل موجود باقياً، فيجب أن يكون كونه باقياً أقنوماً خامساً، ولا جواب لهم عن ذلك، وفيه ترك التثليث .
With two hypostases other than knowledge, it was said to them: Likewise, the knowledge of the Exalted Creator is His life, so it must be that He has two hypostases; and they have no answer for any of that. If one of them says: 'Hypostaticity is only established for the Creator by an attribute related to Himself, not connected to other than Him, and it is His being existent and substance referring to Himself, and His being living referring to Him and not connected to other than Him, and His being knowledgeable by Himself as an attribute referring by it to Himself; and He only has a hypostasis by His being knowledgeable by Himself, not by other than Him.' It is said to them: Likewise, He is eternal by Himself, and not every existing substance is eternal by itself? So it must be that His being eternal is a fourth hypostasis; and likewise His being everlasting is an attribute... It is a thing existing by itself and a substance by itself, so it must be that His being a thing existing is a hypostasis, and His being a substance is a hypostasis, because not every existing substance refers to itself, not connected to other than Him, and not every existing thing is everlasting, so it must be that His being everlasting is a fifth hypostasis, and they have no answer for that, and in it is the abandonment of the Trinity.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer argument against the Christian doctrine of three hypostases (aqānīm). The author presents a Christian claim that divine attributes like knowledge and life are hypostatic attributes pertaining only to God's essence, and then refutes it by showing that this logic leads to an infinite regress of hypostases. The Christian argues that only those attributes that refer solely to God's essence (e.g., being existent, substance, living, knowledgeable) constitute hypostases. The author responds: if that is the case, then His being eternal by Himself, His being everlasting, and even His being a thing and a substance would each have to be a distinct hypostasis, because not all things share these properties. Thus, the Christian would have to posit four or five hypostases, contradicting the doctrine of three. The argument ends by stating that this reasoning leads to abandoning the Trinity entirely.

Misconception: Some might think Baqillani denies that God has attributes like knowledge and life.
Correction: Baqillani is not denying divine attributes; he is showing that the Christian definition of hypostasis leads to an absurd number of hypostases.

B) To show that the Christian logic would require more than three hypostases.
C) To deny that God has attributes like knowledge and life.

The Common Substance Dilemma
A logical objection to the Trinity using the common substance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Islamic theologians exposed logical contradictions in the Christian doctrine of the Trinity by questioning the relationship between the 'common substance' and the three hypostases.

Core Idea
The 'common substance' dilemma shows that the Trinity is logically incoherent.

In this passage, Imam al-Baqillani presents a sharp logical objection to the Christian doctrine of the hypostases (aqānīm). He asks whether the 'common substance' that supposedly underlies the Father, Son, and Holy Spirit is identical to them or distinct. This seemingly simple question reveals a deep inconsistency: if the substance is the same as the hypostases, then they cannot be distinct; if it is different, then God is not one substance. Let's examine how the argument unfolds.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that the text is cut off, but the core question is clear: the author asks about the relationship between the common substance and the hypostases.
The passage ends mid-sentence due to a footnote; the full argument is not present.
2
Identify the two possible answers
The author offers two possible replies: either the common substance is the hypostases or it is not. The Jacobites and Nestorians say it is not other than the hypostases.
This sets up a dilemma.
3
Consider the counter-question
The author then asks: 'Is not the substance undifferentiated...?' This implies that if the substance is the same, then the hypostases cannot have distinct properties.
The argument is incomplete, but the logical trap is evident.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself: why does the author use this line of questioning? It is not to understand Christian doctrine but to show its inherent contradictions.
This is a classical kalam method of refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة عليهم في الأقانيم يقال لهم : خبروني عن الجوهر العام الجامع للأقانيم الذي هذه الأقانيم له أقانيم : أهو عندكم الأقانيم أم غيرها؟ فإن قالت اليعقوبية والنسطورية : ليس الجوهر بغير الأقانيم ، قيل : أفليس الجوهر غير مختلف من حيث كان جوهراً ومن حيث لم يكن معدوداً ومن حيث لم تكن له
A question against them concerning the hypostases: It is said to them: Inform me about the common substance that encompasses the hypostases, which these hypostases have hypostases: Is it, in your view, the hypostases or other than them? If the Jacobites and Nestorians say: 'The substance is not other than the hypostases,' it is said: Is not the substance undifferentiated in terms of being a substance and in terms of not being numbered and in terms of not having?
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This passage introduces a new objection by the author against the Christian doctrine of hypostases. The author asks about the 'common substance' (al-jawhar al-ʿāmm) that encompasses the three hypostases: is this substance identical to the hypostases or distinct from them? He then presents the response of the Jacobites and Nestorians, who assert that the substance is not other than the hypostases. The author's counter-question begins: 'Is not the substance undifferentiated...' but the text breaks off. The implied argument is that if the substance is not distinct from the hypostases, then the hypostases cannot be distinct from each other, or the substance itself would be subject to differentiation, leading to contradictions. This question aims to expose inconsistency in the Christian position regarding the relationship between the one substance and the three hypostases.

Key Terms
جوهر عام
أقانيم
يعقوبية
نسطورية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the author is seeking clarification about Christian theology.
Correction: The author's aim is not to understand but to expose a logical flaw: the relationship between substance and hypostases is incoherent.

Checkpoint
What is the author's aim in asking about the common substance?
A) To determine which Christian sect is correct.
B) To show a logical contradiction in the relationship between the substance and hypostases.
C) To affirm that God is a substance without attributes.
D) To ask for a definition of substance.

Key Takeaway
The 'common substance' dilemma is a powerful argument that the Trinity is self-contradictory because it cannot coherently explain how one substance can be three distinct hypostases.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Core Dilemma: Essence and Hypostases
Baqillani poses the dilemma and records the Jacobite/Nestorian answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the initial logical question that Baqillani poses to Trinitarian theologians, exposing the inherent tension in their beliefs.

Core Idea
If hypostases are the essence, they must be both differentiated and non‑differentiated — a contradiction.

Baqillani opens his refutation by asking a devastatingly simple question: Are the hypostases identical to the essence or distinct from it? The Jacobites and Nestorians answer that the essence is not other than the hypostases. Baqillani then points out that the essence is non‑differentiated, non‑counted, and without distinct properties, while the hypostases are differentiated, counted, and have distinct properties. This sets up the logical contradiction that will be developed later.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening question
Read the Arabic passage asking whether the hypostases are the essence or something else. Notice the direct and challenging tone.
Baqillani uses a rhetorical question to force an answer.
2
Identify the Jacobite/Nestorian response
They claim the essence is not other than the hypostases. Understand what this implies about identity.
3
Contrast the attributes of essence and hypostases
Baqillani then lists attributes: essence is non‑differentiated, non‑counted, without distinct properties; hypostases have opposite attributes. See the tension.
This contrast is the seed of the later contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأقانيم له أقانيم : أهو عندكم الأقانيم أم غيرها؟ فإن قالت اليعقوبية والنسطورية : ليس الجوهر بغير الأقانيم ، قيل : أفليس الجوهر غير مختلف من حيث كان جوهراً ومن حيث لم يكن معدوداً ومن حيث لم تكن له خواص متباينة المعنى ؟
اليعقوبية: وهم أصحاب يعقوب. قالوا بالأقانيم الثلاثة، إلا أنهم قالوا : انقلبت الكلمة لحماً ودماً، فصار الإله هو المسيح. وهو الظاهر بجسده، بل هو هو. وعنهم أخبرنا القرآن الكريم لقد كفر الذين قالوا إن الله هو المسيح ابن مريم فمنهم من قال: إن المسيح الله تعالى. ومنهم من قال ظهر اللاهوت بالناسوت فصار ناسوت المسيح مظهر الجوهرة، لا على طريق حلول جزء فيه، ولا على سبيل اتحاد الكلمة التي هي في حكم الصفة بل صار هو هو. وهذا كما يقال ظهر الملك بصورة إنسان، أو ظهر الشيطان بصورة حيوان وزعم قوم من اليعقوبية أن الكلمة لم تأخذ من مريم شيئاً، ولكنها مرت بها كالماء بالميزاب وما ظهر بها من شخص المسيح في الأعين فهو كالخيال والصورة في المرآة وإلا فما كان جسماً متجسماً كثيفاً في الحقيقة. وكذلك القتل والصلب وإنما وقع على الخيال والحسبان، وهؤلاء يقال لهم الإليانية وهم قوم بالشام واليمن وأرمينية قالوا : إنما صلب الإله أحلنا من حتى يخلصنا. وزعم بعضهم أن الكلمة كانت تدخل جسم المسيح عليه السلام أحياناً، فتصدر عنه الآيات من إحياء الموتى، وإبراء الأكمه والأبرص وتفارقه في بعض الأوقات فترد عليه الآلام والأوجاع.
النسطورية: أصحاب نسطور وقد تصرف في الأناجيل بحكم رأيه وإضافته إليهم إضافة المعتزلة إلى هذه الشريعة قال : إن الله تعالى واحد ذو أقانيم ثلاثة الوجود والعلم والحياة، وهذه الأقانيم ليست زائدة على الذات ولا هي هو واتحدت الكلمة بجسد عيسى عليه السلام، لا على طريقة الامتزاج كما قالت الملكانية، ولا على طريقة الظهورية كما قالت اليعقوبية ولكن كإشراق الشمس في كوة على بلورة، وكظهور النقش في الشمع إذا طبع الخاتم وأشبه المذاهب بمذهب نسطور في الأقانيم : أحوال أبي هاشم من المعتزلة، فإنه يثبت خواص مختلفة لشيء واحد ويعني بقوله واحد يعني الإله . قال : هو واحد بالجوهر. أي ليس هو مركبا من جنسين بل هو بسيط وواحد. ويعني بالحياة والعلم اقنومين جوهرين، أي أصلين مبدأين للعالم. ثم فسر العلم بالنطق والكلمة . ويرجع منتهى كلامه إلى إثبات كونه تعالى موجوداً، حياً، ناطقاً كما تقول الفلاسفة في أحد الإنسان إلا أن هذه المعاني تتغاير في الإنسان ككونه جوهراً مركباً. وهو جوهر بسيط غير مركب. ومن النسطورية قوم يقال لهم المصلين قالوا في المسيح مثل ما قال نسطور إلا أنهم قالوا : إذا اجتهد الرجل في العبادة، وترك التغذي باللحم والدسم، ورفض الشهوات الحيوانية والنفسانية، تصفي جوهره حتى يبلغ ملكوت السموات ويرى الله تعالى جهرة وينكشف له ما في الغيب فلا تخفى عليه خافية الأرض ولا في السماء. ومن النسطورية من ينفي التشبيه، ويثبت القول بالقدر خيره وشره من العبد كما قالت القدرية.
ثم قيل لهم : أفليس الأقانيم مختلفة من حيث هي خواص متباينة المعنى، ومن حيث هي معدودة، ومن حيث هي أقانيم، ومن حيث أن الابن منها تدرع واتحد بجسد المسيح عليه السلام دون الرُّوح ؟ فإن قالوا : نعم، ولا بد من ذلك، قيل لهم : فإذا كان الجوهر هو الأقانيم والأقانيم مختلفة معدودة متباينة في الاختصاص، ومنها المتحد وهي نفس الجوهر، فنفس الجوهر إذاً مختلفة معدودة متباينة متحدة بناسوت المسيح عليه السلام فيجب أن يكون نفس الجوهر الذي ليس بمعدودٍ ولا مختلف ولا متحدٍ ولا متباين المعنى هو نفس المختلف المعدود المتباين المعنى المتحد؛ وهذا جهل ممن صار إليه وليس ذلك قولهم في الجوهر ؛ ولا خلاص لهم منه.
فإن قالت الملكية منهم، وهم الروم : إن الجوهر غير الأقانيم، قيل لهم : فإذا كان الجوهر إلها، والأقانيم الثلاثة آلهة وهي غيره، فالآلهة إذاً أربعة : جوهر وثلاثة أقانيم غيره؛ وهذا يبطل قولكم بالتثليث. وإن قالوا : الآلهة ثلاثة أقانيم، والرابع جوهر ليس بإله غير الثلاثة، قيل لهم : فلا فرق إذاً بين قول الأقانيم ثلاثة ولا جوهر هناك يجمعها وتكون له، وبين قول : إن هناك ثلاثة أقانيم وجوهراً جامعاً لها؛ فيجب أن يكون وجود الرابع كعدمه وإثباته كنفيه؛ وهذا جهل ممن صار إليه.
The hypostases have hypostases: Is it in your view that they are the hypostases or other than them? If the Jacobites and Nestorians say: The essence is not other than the hypostases, it is said: Is not the essence non-different in that it is an essence, and in that it is not counted, and in that it does not have mutually distinct properties? The Jacobites: They are the followers of Jacob. They affirmed the three hypostases, except that they said: The Word turned into flesh and blood, so God became the Messiah. He is apparent with His body, rather He is He. And from them the noble Quran told us: 'Certainly disbelieved those who said that God is the Messiah, son of Mary.' Some of them said: The Messiah is God Almighty. Some of them said: The divinity appeared in the humanity, so the humanity of the Messiah became a manifestation of the essence, not by way of indwelling of a part in it, nor by way of union of the Word which is in the status of an attribute, but He became He. This is like saying the king appears in the form of a man, or the devil appears in the form of an animal. And a group of the Jacobites claimed that the Word did not take anything from Mary, but it passed through her like water through a spout, and what appeared of the person of the Messiah in the eyes is like an illusion and an image in a mirror; otherwise, it was not a thick, embodied body in reality. Likewise, the killing and crucifixion only occurred upon illusion and imagination. These are called the Elianites, and they are a people in Syria, Yemen, and Armenia. They said: The god was crucified to atone for us so that He might save us. And some of them claimed that the Word used to enter the body of the Messiah, peace be upon him, sometimes, and miracles would issue from him, such as reviving the dead, healing the blind and leper, and it would leave him at other times, so pains and ailments would return to him. The Nestorians: They are the followers of Nestorius, who manipulated the Gospels according to his opinion and added to them as the Mu'tazilites added to this Sharia. He said: God Almighty is one, possessing three hypostases: existence, knowledge, and life. These hypostases are not additional to the essence nor are they identical with it. The Word united with the body of Jesus, peace be upon him, not by way of mixing as the Melkites said, nor by way of manifestation as the Jacobites said, but like the shining of the sun through a skylight onto a crystal, and like the appearance of an engraving in wax when stamped with a seal. The school of Nestorius regarding the hypostases resembles the states of Abu Hashim from the Mu'tazilites, for he affirms different properties for one thing. By 'one' he means God. He said: He is one in essence, meaning He is not composed of two kinds but is simple and one. He means by life and knowledge two essential hypostases, i.e., two origins, two principles of the world. Then he interpreted knowledge as speech and word. The conclusion of his speech returns to affirming that He, exalted, is existent, living, speaking, as the philosophers say about any human, except that these meanings differ in the human as he is a composite essence. He is a simple essence, not composite. Among the Nestorians are a people called the Prayers, who said about the Messiah like what Nestorius said, except they said: When a man strives in worship, abandons eating meat and fat, and rejects animal and soulful desires, his essence becomes purified until he reaches the kingdom of the heavens and sees God Almighty openly, and what is in the unseen is revealed to him, so no hidden thing on earth or in heaven is hidden from him. Among the Nestorians are those who negate anthropomorphism and affirm the doctrine of predestination, its good and evil, from the servant, as the Qadariyya said. Then it was said to them: Are not the hypostases different in that they are mutually distinct properties, and in that they are counted, and in that they are hypostases, and in that the Son among them put on armor and united with the body of the Messiah, peace be upon him, without the Spirit? If they say: Yes, and that is necessary, it is said to them: If the essence is the hypostases, and the hypostases are different, counted, distinct in specificity, and among them is the one that united, and it is the essence itself, then the essence itself is therefore different, counted, distinct, united with the humanity of the Messiah, peace be upon him. So it must be that the essence itself which is not counted, not different, not united, and not of distinct meaning is the same as the different, counted, distinct-in-meaning, united one. This is ignorance on the part of whoever holds it, and that is not their statement about the essence, and there is no escape from it for them. If the Melkites among them, who are the Romans, say: The essence is other than the hypostases, it is said to them: If the essence is a god, and the three hypostases are gods and are other than it, then the gods are four: an essence and three hypostases other than it. This invalidates your doctrine of trinity. And if they say: The gods are three hypostases, and the fourth is an essence that is not a god other than the three, it is said to them: There is no difference then between saying 'three hypostases and no essence that encompasses them and belongs to them' and saying 'there are three hypostases and an encompassing essence for them'. So the existence of the fourth must be like its non-existence, and its affirmation like its negation. This is ignorance on the part of whoever holds it.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Christian Trinitarian doctrines concerning the hypostases (aqanim) and the essence (jawhar). Baqillani begins by posing a key question: In your view, are the hypostases identical to the essence or distinct from it? He then addresses two main positions. First, the Jacobites and Nestorians claim that the essence is not other than the hypostases. Baqillani first provides a detailed account of each sect's beliefs: the Jacobites hold that the Word became flesh and that the divine and human are united in such a way that the divine is manifested through the human, while the Nestorians affirm three hypostases (existence, knowledge, life) and a union of the Word with the body of Jesus like the shining of sunlight or the impression of a seal. He then proceeds to the logical refutation. He asks: Is not the essence non-differentiated, non-countable, without mutually distinct properties? They must agree. Then he asks: Are not the hypostases different (as distinct properties), countable, hypostases, and the Son is said to have taken flesh and united with Christ to the exclusion of the Spirit? They agree again. Then follows the contradiction: If the essence is the hypostases, and the hypostases are different, countable, distinct, and one of them is united, then the essence itself must possess all those attributes (different, countable, distinct, united). Yet the essence is also supposed to be without these attributes (non-differentiated, non-countable, etc.). Thus the same entity would have contradictory properties, which is absurd. Hence their position is untenable. Second, Baqillani addresses the Melkites (the Romans) who say the essence is other than the hypostases. If the essence is a god and the three hypostases are gods distinct from it, then there would be four gods, contradicting the doctrine of trinity. If they instead claim that only the three hypostases are gods and the fourth (the essence) is not a god, then that essence is redundant and adds nothing; its existence is equivalent to non-existence. Thus their view also collapses. The passage demonstrates Baqillani's method of exposing internal inconsistencies in opposing doctrines without relying on scriptural authority.

Key Terms
الأقانيم
الجوهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What do the Jacobites and Nestorians say about the relationship between the essence and the hypostases?
A) The essence is other than the hypostases.
B) The essence is not other than the hypostases.
C) The essence is only one of the hypostases.
D) The essence is unknowable.

Key Takeaway
The identity of essence and hypostases leads to a contradiction, because the essence is undifferentiated while the hypostases are differentiated.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Baqillani forces his interlocutor to face a logical contradiction. When you hold a belief that feels comfortable, do you ever stop to examine whether it contains hidden inconsistencies? What belief in your own life might need such scrutiny?
?
The Jacobites and Nestorians replied honestly, yet their answer led to a dead end. In your own faith, are you more concerned with being right or with following truth wherever it leads, even if it means admitting a contradiction?
?
If you were standing before Baqillani and he asked you whether the hypostases are the essence or not, could you answer without contradicting yourself? What would your answer reveal about how deeply you think about your beliefs?
