Sects and Disagreements
intermediate
8 min
Jacobite Christology: The Word Becomes Flesh
Baqillani details the Jacobite views on the incarnation and the nature of Christ.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Jacobite doctrine of the hypostases, including their view that the Word turned into flesh and that the divinity appeared in humanity.

Core Idea
The Jacobites believed the Word literally became flesh, so the Messiah is God himself manifested.

Having posed the initial question, Baqillani now describes the specific beliefs of the Jacobite sect. They hold that the Word transformed into flesh and blood, making the Messiah identical to God. He also recounts their various interpretations, including the idea that the Word passed through Mary like water through a spout, and that the crucifixion was only an illusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the Jacobite belief summary
Read the passage describing the basic Jacobite position: the Word turned into flesh and the Messiah is God.
Notice the Quranic reference they claimed support from.
2
Identify the two sub‑interpretations
The passage presents two subgroups: one says divinity appeared in humanity (manifestation), another says the Word passed through Mary without taking anything.
The second group is called the Elianites.
3
Note the view on crucifixion
Some Jacobites claimed the crucifixion was only an illusion, and some said the Word entered and left the body of Christ.
This shows the variety within the sect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأقانيم له أقانيم : أهو عندكم الأقانيم أم غيرها؟ فإن قالت اليعقوبية والنسطورية : ليس الجوهر بغير الأقانيم ، قيل : أفليس الجوهر غير مختلف من حيث كان جوهراً ومن حيث لم يكن معدوداً ومن حيث لم تكن له خواص متباينة المعنى ؟
اليعقوبية: وهم أصحاب يعقوب. قالوا بالأقانيم الثلاثة، إلا أنهم قالوا : انقلبت الكلمة لحماً ودماً، فصار الإله هو المسيح. وهو الظاهر بجسده، بل هو هو. وعنهم أخبرنا القرآن الكريم لقد كفر الذين قالوا إن الله هو المسيح ابن مريم فمنهم من قال: إن المسيح الله تعالى. ومنهم من قال ظهر اللاهوت بالناسوت فصار ناسوت المسيح مظهر الجوهرة، لا على طريق حلول جزء فيه، ولا على سبيل اتحاد الكلمة التي هي في حكم الصفة بل صار هو هو. وهذا كما يقال ظهر الملك بصورة إنسان، أو ظهر الشيطان بصورة حيوان وزعم قوم من اليعقوبية أن الكلمة لم تأخذ من مريم شيئاً، ولكنها مرت بها كالماء بالميزاب وما ظهر بها من شخص المسيح في الأعين فهو كالخيال والصورة في المرآة وإلا فما كان جسماً متجسماً كثيفاً في الحقيقة. وكذلك القتل والصلب وإنما وقع على الخيال والحسبان، وهؤلاء يقال لهم الإليانية وهم قوم بالشام واليمن وأرمينية قالوا : إنما صلب الإله أحلنا من حتى يخلصنا. وزعم بعضهم أن الكلمة كانت تدخل جسم المسيح عليه السلام أحياناً، فتصدر عنه الآيات من إحياء الموتى، وإبراء الأكمه والأبرص وتفارقه في بعض الأوقات فترد عليه الآلام والأوجاع.
النسطورية: أصحاب نسطور وقد تصرف في الأناجيل بحكم رأيه وإضافته إليهم إضافة المعتزلة إلى هذه الشريعة قال : إن الله تعالى واحد ذو أقانيم ثلاثة الوجود والعلم والحياة، وهذه الأقانيم ليست زائدة على الذات ولا هي هو واتحدت الكلمة بجسد عيسى عليه السلام، لا على طريقة الامتزاج كما قالت الملكانية، ولا على طريقة الظهورية كما قالت اليعقوبية ولكن كإشراق الشمس في كوة على بلورة، وكظهور النقش في الشمع إذا طبع الخاتم وأشبه المذاهب بمذهب نسطور في الأقانيم : أحوال أبي هاشم من المعتزلة، فإنه يثبت خواص مختلفة لشيء واحد ويعني بقوله واحد يعني الإله . قال : هو واحد بالجوهر. أي ليس هو مركبا من جنسين بل هو بسيط وواحد. ويعني بالحياة والعلم اقنومين جوهرين، أي أصلين مبدأين للعالم. ثم فسر العلم بالنطق والكلمة . ويرجع منتهى كلامه إلى إثبات كونه تعالى موجوداً، حياً، ناطقاً كما تقول الفلاسفة في أحد الإنسان إلا أن هذه المعاني تتغاير في الإنسان ككونه جوهراً مركباً. وهو جوهر بسيط غير مركب. ومن النسطورية قوم يقال لهم المصلين قالوا في المسيح مثل ما قال نسطور إلا أنهم قالوا : إذا اجتهد الرجل في العبادة، وترك التغذي باللحم والدسم، ورفض الشهوات الحيوانية والنفسانية، تصفي جوهره حتى يبلغ ملكوت السموات ويرى الله تعالى جهرة وينكشف له ما في الغيب فلا تخفى عليه خافية الأرض ولا في السماء. ومن النسطورية من ينفي التشبيه، ويثبت القول بالقدر خيره وشره من العبد كما قالت القدرية.
ثم قيل لهم : أفليس الأقانيم مختلفة من حيث هي خواص متباينة المعنى، ومن حيث هي معدودة، ومن حيث هي أقانيم، ومن حيث أن الابن منها تدرع واتحد بجسد المسيح عليه السلام دون الرُّوح ؟ فإن قالوا : نعم، ولا بد من ذلك، قيل لهم : فإذا كان الجوهر هو الأقانيم والأقانيم مختلفة معدودة متباينة في الاختصاص، ومنها المتحد وهي نفس الجوهر، فنفس الجوهر إذاً مختلفة معدودة متباينة متحدة بناسوت المسيح عليه السلام فيجب أن يكون نفس الجوهر الذي ليس بمعدودٍ ولا مختلف ولا متحدٍ ولا متباين المعنى هو نفس المختلف المعدود المتباين المعنى المتحد؛ وهذا جهل ممن صار إليه وليس ذلك قولهم في الجوهر ؛ ولا خلاص لهم منه.
فإن قالت الملكية منهم، وهم الروم : إن الجوهر غير الأقانيم، قيل لهم : فإذا كان الجوهر إلها، والأقانيم الثلاثة آلهة وهي غيره، فالآلهة إذاً أربعة : جوهر وثلاثة أقانيم غيره؛ وهذا يبطل قولكم بالتثليث. وإن قالوا : الآلهة ثلاثة أقانيم، والرابع جوهر ليس بإله غير الثلاثة، قيل لهم : فلا فرق إذاً بين قول الأقانيم ثلاثة ولا جوهر هناك يجمعها وتكون له، وبين قول : إن هناك ثلاثة أقانيم وجوهراً جامعاً لها؛ فيجب أن يكون وجود الرابع كعدمه وإثباته كنفيه؛ وهذا جهل ممن صار إليه.
The hypostases have hypostases: Is it in your view that they are the hypostases or other than them? If the Jacobites and Nestorians say: The essence is not other than the hypostases, it is said: Is not the essence non-different in that it is an essence, and in that it is not counted, and in that it does not have mutually distinct properties? The Jacobites: They are the followers of Jacob. They affirmed the three hypostases, except that they said: The Word turned into flesh and blood, so God became the Messiah. He is apparent with His body, rather He is He. And from them the noble Quran told us: 'Certainly disbelieved those who said that God is the Messiah, son of Mary.' Some of them said: The Messiah is God Almighty. Some of them said: The divinity appeared in the humanity, so the humanity of the Messiah became a manifestation of the essence, not by way of indwelling of a part in it, nor by way of union of the Word which is in the status of an attribute, but He became He. This is like saying the king appears in the form of a man, or the devil appears in the form of an animal. And a group of the Jacobites claimed that the Word did not take anything from Mary, but it passed through her like water through a spout, and what appeared of the person of the Messiah in the eyes is like an illusion and an image in a mirror; otherwise, it was not a thick, embodied body in reality. Likewise, the killing and crucifixion only occurred upon illusion and imagination. These are called the Elianites, and they are a people in Syria, Yemen, and Armenia. They said: The god was crucified to atone for us so that He might save us. And some of them claimed that the Word used to enter the body of the Messiah, peace be upon him, sometimes, and miracles would issue from him, such as reviving the dead, healing the blind and leper, and it would leave him at other times, so pains and ailments would return to him. The Nestorians: They are the followers of Nestorius, who manipulated the Gospels according to his opinion and added to them as the Mu'tazilites added to this Sharia. He said: God Almighty is one, possessing three hypostases: existence, knowledge, and life. These hypostases are not additional to the essence nor are they identical with it. The Word united with the body of Jesus, peace be upon him, not by way of mixing as the Melkites said, nor by way of manifestation as the Jacobites said, but like the shining of the sun through a skylight onto a crystal, and like the appearance of an engraving in wax when stamped with a seal. The school of Nestorius regarding the hypostases resembles the states of Abu Hashim from the Mu'tazilites, for he affirms different properties for one thing. By 'one' he means God. He said: He is one in essence, meaning He is not composed of two kinds but is simple and one. He means by life and knowledge two essential hypostases, i.e., two origins, two principles of the world. Then he interpreted knowledge as speech and word. The conclusion of his speech returns to affirming that He, exalted, is existent, living, speaking, as the philosophers say about any human, except that these meanings differ in the human as he is a composite essence. He is a simple essence, not composite. Among the Nestorians are a people called the Prayers, who said about the Messiah like what Nestorius said, except they said: When a man strives in worship, abandons eating meat and fat, and rejects animal and soulful desires, his essence becomes purified until he reaches the kingdom of the heavens and sees God Almighty openly, and what is in the unseen is revealed to him, so no hidden thing on earth or in heaven is hidden from him. Among the Nestorians are those who negate anthropomorphism and affirm the doctrine of predestination, its good and evil, from the servant, as the Qadariyya said. Then it was said to them: Are not the hypostases different in that they are mutually distinct properties, and in that they are counted, and in that they are hypostases, and in that the Son among them put on armor and united with the body of the Messiah, peace be upon him, without the Spirit? If they say: Yes, and that is necessary, it is said to them: If the essence is the hypostases, and the hypostases are different, counted, distinct in specificity, and among them is the one that united, and it is the essence itself, then the essence itself is therefore different, counted, distinct, united with the humanity of the Messiah, peace be upon him. So it must be that the essence itself which is not counted, not different, not united, and not of distinct meaning is the same as the different, counted, distinct-in-meaning, united one. This is ignorance on the part of whoever holds it, and that is not their statement about the essence, and there is no escape from it for them. If the Melkites among them, who are the Romans, say: The essence is other than the hypostases, it is said to them: If the essence is a god, and the three hypostases are gods and are other than it, then the gods are four: an essence and three hypostases other than it. This invalidates your doctrine of trinity. And if they say: The gods are three hypostases, and the fourth is an essence that is not a god other than the three, it is said to them: There is no difference then between saying 'three hypostases and no essence that encompasses them and belongs to them' and saying 'there are three hypostases and an encompassing essence for them'. So the existence of the fourth must be like its non-existence, and its affirmation like its negation. This is ignorance on the part of whoever holds it.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Christian Trinitarian doctrines concerning the hypostases (aqanim) and the essence (jawhar). Baqillani begins by posing a key question: In your view, are the hypostases identical to the essence or distinct from it? He then addresses two main positions. First, the Jacobites and Nestorians claim that the essence is not other than the hypostases. Baqillani first provides a detailed account of each sect's beliefs: the Jacobites hold that the Word became flesh and that the divine and human are united in such a way that the divine is manifested through the human, while the Nestorians affirm three hypostases (existence, knowledge, life) and a union of the Word with the body of Jesus like the shining of sunlight or the impression of a seal. He then proceeds to the logical refutation. He asks: Is not the essence non-differentiated, non-countable, without mutually distinct properties? They must agree. Then he asks: Are not the hypostases different (as distinct properties), countable, hypostases, and the Son is said to have taken flesh and united with Christ to the exclusion of the Spirit? They agree again. Then follows the contradiction: If the essence is the hypostases, and the hypostases are different, countable, distinct, and one of them is united, then the essence itself must possess all those attributes (different, countable, distinct, united). Yet the essence is also supposed to be without these attributes (non-differentiated, non-countable, etc.). Thus the same entity would have contradictory properties, which is absurd. Hence their position is untenable. Second, Baqillani addresses the Melkites (the Romans) who say the essence is other than the hypostases. If the essence is a god and the three hypostases are gods distinct from it, then there would be four gods, contradicting the doctrine of trinity. If they instead claim that only the three hypostases are gods and the fourth (the essence) is not a god, then that essence is redundant and adds nothing; its existence is equivalent to non-existence. Thus their view also collapses. The passage demonstrates Baqillani's method of exposing internal inconsistencies in opposing doctrines without relying on scriptural authority.

الكلمة
الناسوت
اللاهوت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think all Jacobites held a single, unified doctrine on the incarnation.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the Jacobites were divided into at least three distinct subgroups, each with different explanations of how the Word related to Christ's body.

Checkpoint
What did the Elianite subgroup of Jacobites believe about the crucifixion?
A) It was a real, physical event.
B) It was an illusion and only appeared to happen.
C) It was only a spiritual crucifixion.
D) It did not happen at all.

Key Takeaway
The Jacobites had several conflicting interpretations of how the Word became flesh, revealing the instability of their doctrine.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the Quran's warning against those who say 'God is the Messiah,' do you ever catch yourself thinking of Jesus in ways that blur the line between human and Divine—how would you defend Islamic monotheism if challenged by a Christian?
?
The Jacobite belief that the Word passed through Mary like water through a spout reduces the Messiah to a mere apparition. Are there ways you might be treating your own faith or actions as mere appearances—going through the motions without real substance?
?
The Elianites claimed the crucifixion was an illusion to avoid the shame of the cross. Is there a painful reality in your life that you are tempted to treat as unreal to avoid confronting it?

Nestorian Doctrine: Union Without Mixing
Baqillani details the Nestorian views on the hypostases and the union of the Word with Christ.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Nestorian view of the Trinity and the union of the Word with Christ, as well as its resemblance to the Mu'tazilite theory of states (ahwal).

Core Idea
Nestorius taught a union of the Word with Christ like sunlight on a crystal, not by mixture or manifestation.

Baqillani then turns to the Nestorians, followers of Nestorius. They affirm three hypostases (existence, knowledge, life) and describe the union of the Word with Jesus as an intimate connection without mixing or manifestation. Baqillani notes the similarity to Abu Hashim's theory of states, and also mentions other Nestorian subgroups.

Guided Path
1
Read the Nestorian belief summary
Read the passage about Nestorius's doctrine: three hypostases (existence, knowledge, life) and the union of the Word with Christ.
Notice the analogy of sunlight shining through a skylight onto a crystal.
2
Compare with Mu'tazilite states
Baqillani points out the similarity to Abu Hashim's theory of states (ahwal). Understand why he makes this comparison.
This shows the philosophical influences on Nestorianism.
3
Identify the sub‑sects
The passage mentions a group called 'the Prayers' and another that negates anthropomorphism and affirms predestination.
These show further fragmentation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأقانيم له أقانيم : أهو عندكم الأقانيم أم غيرها؟ فإن قالت اليعقوبية والنسطورية : ليس الجوهر بغير الأقانيم ، قيل : أفليس الجوهر غير مختلف من حيث كان جوهراً ومن حيث لم يكن معدوداً ومن حيث لم تكن له خواص متباينة المعنى ؟
اليعقوبية: وهم أصحاب يعقوب. قالوا بالأقانيم الثلاثة، إلا أنهم قالوا : انقلبت الكلمة لحماً ودماً، فصار الإله هو المسيح. وهو الظاهر بجسده، بل هو هو. وعنهم أخبرنا القرآن الكريم لقد كفر الذين قالوا إن الله هو المسيح ابن مريم فمنهم من قال: إن المسيح الله تعالى. ومنهم من قال ظهر اللاهوت بالناسوت فصار ناسوت المسيح مظهر الجوهرة، لا على طريق حلول جزء فيه، ولا على سبيل اتحاد الكلمة التي هي في حكم الصفة بل صار هو هو. وهذا كما يقال ظهر الملك بصورة إنسان، أو ظهر الشيطان بصورة حيوان وزعم قوم من اليعقوبية أن الكلمة لم تأخذ من مريم شيئاً، ولكنها مرت بها كالماء بالميزاب وما ظهر بها من شخص المسيح في الأعين فهو كالخيال والصورة في المرآة وإلا فما كان جسماً متجسماً كثيفاً في الحقيقة. وكذلك القتل والصلب وإنما وقع على الخيال والحسبان، وهؤلاء يقال لهم الإليانية وهم قوم بالشام واليمن وأرمينية قالوا : إنما صلب الإله أحلنا من حتى يخلصنا. وزعم بعضهم أن الكلمة كانت تدخل جسم المسيح عليه السلام أحياناً، فتصدر عنه الآيات من إحياء الموتى، وإبراء الأكمه والأبرص وتفارقه في بعض الأوقات فترد عليه الآلام والأوجاع.
النسطورية: أصحاب نسطور وقد تصرف في الأناجيل بحكم رأيه وإضافته إليهم إضافة المعتزلة إلى هذه الشريعة قال : إن الله تعالى واحد ذو أقانيم ثلاثة الوجود والعلم والحياة، وهذه الأقانيم ليست زائدة على الذات ولا هي هو واتحدت الكلمة بجسد عيسى عليه السلام، لا على طريقة الامتزاج كما قالت الملكانية، ولا على طريقة الظهورية كما قالت اليعقوبية ولكن كإشراق الشمس في كوة على بلورة، وكظهور النقش في الشمع إذا طبع الخاتم وأشبه المذاهب بمذهب نسطور في الأقانيم : أحوال أبي هاشم من المعتزلة، فإنه يثبت خواص مختلفة لشيء واحد ويعني بقوله واحد يعني الإله . قال : هو واحد بالجوهر. أي ليس هو مركبا من جنسين بل هو بسيط وواحد. ويعني بالحياة والعلم اقنومين جوهرين، أي أصلين مبدأين للعالم. ثم فسر العلم بالنطق والكلمة . ويرجع منتهى كلامه إلى إثبات كونه تعالى موجوداً، حياً، ناطقاً كما تقول الفلاسفة في أحد الإنسان إلا أن هذه المعاني تتغاير في الإنسان ككونه جوهراً مركباً. وهو جوهر بسيط غير مركب. ومن النسطورية قوم يقال لهم المصلين قالوا في المسيح مثل ما قال نسطور إلا أنهم قالوا : إذا اجتهد الرجل في العبادة، وترك التغذي باللحم والدسم، ورفض الشهوات الحيوانية والنفسانية، تصفي جوهره حتى يبلغ ملكوت السموات ويرى الله تعالى جهرة وينكشف له ما في الغيب فلا تخفى عليه خافية الأرض ولا في السماء. ومن النسطورية من ينفي التشبيه، ويثبت القول بالقدر خيره وشره من العبد كما قالت القدرية.
ثم قيل لهم : أفليس الأقانيم مختلفة من حيث هي خواص متباينة المعنى، ومن حيث هي معدودة، ومن حيث هي أقانيم، ومن حيث أن الابن منها تدرع واتحد بجسد المسيح عليه السلام دون الرُّوح ؟ فإن قالوا : نعم، ولا بد من ذلك، قيل لهم : فإذا كان الجوهر هو الأقانيم والأقانيم مختلفة معدودة متباينة في الاختصاص، ومنها المتحد وهي نفس الجوهر، فنفس الجوهر إذاً مختلفة معدودة متباينة متحدة بناسوت المسيح عليه السلام فيجب أن يكون نفس الجوهر الذي ليس بمعدودٍ ولا مختلف ولا متحدٍ ولا متباين المعنى هو نفس المختلف المعدود المتباين المعنى المتحد؛ وهذا جهل ممن صار إليه وليس ذلك قولهم في الجوهر ؛ ولا خلاص لهم منه.
فإن قالت الملكية منهم، وهم الروم : إن الجوهر غير الأقانيم، قيل لهم : فإذا كان الجوهر إلها، والأقانيم الثلاثة آلهة وهي غيره، فالآلهة إذاً أربعة : جوهر وثلاثة أقانيم غيره؛ وهذا يبطل قولكم بالتثليث. وإن قالوا : الآلهة ثلاثة أقانيم، والرابع جوهر ليس بإله غير الثلاثة، قيل لهم : فلا فرق إذاً بين قول الأقانيم ثلاثة ولا جوهر هناك يجمعها وتكون له، وبين قول : إن هناك ثلاثة أقانيم وجوهراً جامعاً لها؛ فيجب أن يكون وجود الرابع كعدمه وإثباته كنفيه؛ وهذا جهل ممن صار إليه.
The hypostases have hypostases: Is it in your view that they are the hypostases or other than them? If the Jacobites and Nestorians say: The essence is not other than the hypostases, it is said: Is not the essence non-different in that it is an essence, and in that it is not counted, and in that it does not have mutually distinct properties? The Jacobites: They are the followers of Jacob. They affirmed the three hypostases, except that they said: The Word turned into flesh and blood, so God became the Messiah. He is apparent with His body, rather He is He. And from them the noble Quran told us: 'Certainly disbelieved those who said that God is the Messiah, son of Mary.' Some of them said: The Messiah is God Almighty. Some of them said: The divinity appeared in the humanity, so the humanity of the Messiah became a manifestation of the essence, not by way of indwelling of a part in it, nor by way of union of the Word which is in the status of an attribute, but He became He. This is like saying the king appears in the form of a man, or the devil appears in the form of an animal. And a group of the Jacobites claimed that the Word did not take anything from Mary, but it passed through her like water through a spout, and what appeared of the person of the Messiah in the eyes is like an illusion and an image in a mirror; otherwise, it was not a thick, embodied body in reality. Likewise, the killing and crucifixion only occurred upon illusion and imagination. These are called the Elianites, and they are a people in Syria, Yemen, and Armenia. They said: The god was crucified to atone for us so that He might save us. And some of them claimed that the Word used to enter the body of the Messiah, peace be upon him, sometimes, and miracles would issue from him, such as reviving the dead, healing the blind and leper, and it would leave him at other times, so pains and ailments would return to him. The Nestorians: They are the followers of Nestorius, who manipulated the Gospels according to his opinion and added to them as the Mu'tazilites added to this Sharia. He said: God Almighty is one, possessing three hypostases: existence, knowledge, and life. These hypostases are not additional to the essence nor are they identical with it. The Word united with the body of Jesus, peace be upon him, not by way of mixing as the Melkites said, nor by way of manifestation as the Jacobites said, but like the shining of the sun through a skylight onto a crystal, and like the appearance of an engraving in wax when stamped with a seal. The school of Nestorius regarding the hypostases resembles the states of Abu Hashim from the Mu'tazilites, for he affirms different properties for one thing. By 'one' he means God. He said: He is one in essence, meaning He is not composed of two kinds but is simple and one. He means by life and knowledge two essential hypostases, i.e., two origins, two principles of the world. Then he interpreted knowledge as speech and word. The conclusion of his speech returns to affirming that He, exalted, is existent, living, speaking, as the philosophers say about any human, except that these meanings differ in the human as he is a composite essence. He is a simple essence, not composite. Among the Nestorians are a people called the Prayers, who said about the Messiah like what Nestorius said, except they said: When a man strives in worship, abandons eating meat and fat, and rejects animal and soulful desires, his essence becomes purified until he reaches the kingdom of the heavens and sees God Almighty openly, and what is in the unseen is revealed to him, so no hidden thing on earth or in heaven is hidden from him. Among the Nestorians are those who negate anthropomorphism and affirm the doctrine of predestination, its good and evil, from the servant, as the Qadariyya said. Then it was said to them: Are not the hypostases different in that they are mutually distinct properties, and in that they are counted, and in that they are hypostases, and in that the Son among them put on armor and united with the body of the Messiah, peace be upon him, without the Spirit? If they say: Yes, and that is necessary, it is said to them: If the essence is the hypostases, and the hypostases are different, counted, distinct in specificity, and among them is the one that united, and it is the essence itself, then the essence itself is therefore different, counted, distinct, united with the humanity of the Messiah, peace be upon him. So it must be that the essence itself which is not counted, not different, not united, and not of distinct meaning is the same as the different, counted, distinct-in-meaning, united one. This is ignorance on the part of whoever holds it, and that is not their statement about the essence, and there is no escape from it for them. If the Melkites among them, who are the Romans, say: The essence is other than the hypostases, it is said to them: If the essence is a god, and the three hypostases are gods and are other than it, then the gods are four: an essence and three hypostases other than it. This invalidates your doctrine of trinity. And if they say: The gods are three hypostases, and the fourth is an essence that is not a god other than the three, it is said to them: There is no difference then between saying 'three hypostases and no essence that encompasses them and belongs to them' and saying 'there are three hypostases and an encompassing essence for them'. So the existence of the fourth must be like its non-existence, and its affirmation like its negation. This is ignorance on the part of whoever holds it.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Christian Trinitarian doctrines concerning the hypostases (aqanim) and the essence (jawhar). Baqillani begins by posing a key question: In your view, are the hypostases identical to the essence or distinct from it? He then addresses two main positions. First, the Jacobites and Nestorians claim that the essence is not other than the hypostases. Baqillani first provides a detailed account of each sect's beliefs: the Jacobites hold that the Word became flesh and that the divine and human are united in such a way that the divine is manifested through the human, while the Nestorians affirm three hypostases (existence, knowledge, life) and a union of the Word with the body of Jesus like the shining of sunlight or the impression of a seal. He then proceeds to the logical refutation. He asks: Is not the essence non-differentiated, non-countable, without mutually distinct properties? They must agree. Then he asks: Are not the hypostases different (as distinct properties), countable, hypostases, and the Son is said to have taken flesh and united with Christ to the exclusion of the Spirit? They agree again. Then follows the contradiction: If the essence is the hypostases, and the hypostases are different, countable, distinct, and one of them is united, then the essence itself must possess all those attributes (different, countable, distinct, united). Yet the essence is also supposed to be without these attributes (non-differentiated, non-countable, etc.). Thus the same entity would have contradictory properties, which is absurd. Hence their position is untenable. Second, Baqillani addresses the Melkites (the Romans) who say the essence is other than the hypostases. If the essence is a god and the three hypostases are gods distinct from it, then there would be four gods, contradicting the doctrine of trinity. If they instead claim that only the three hypostases are gods and the fourth (the essence) is not a god, then that essence is redundant and adds nothing; its existence is equivalent to non-existence. Thus their view also collapses. The passage demonstrates Baqillani's method of exposing internal inconsistencies in opposing doctrines without relying on scriptural authority.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think Nestorius's union of the Word with Christ is identical to the Jacobite or Melkite views.
Correction: Baqillani clearly distinguishes Nestorian union as neither mixing (Melkite) nor manifestation (Jacobite), but as a third type akin to sunlight on crystal.

Checkpoint

A) Wasil ibn Ata

Key Takeaway
Nestorius advocated a union of the Word with Christ that is neither mixing nor manifestation, resembling the Mu'tazilite theory of states.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Nestorians claimed to uphold God's oneness yet introduced distinctions that ultimately compromised it. In your own life, do you ever try to reconcile contradictory beliefs about Allah by using intellectual gymnastics, all while claiming to follow revelation? Where might you be prioritizing your reasoning over a clear text?
?
The 'Prayers' subgroup believed extreme asceticism could purify the soul to see Allah directly. Are there any religious practices you perform that you secretly think earn you special access to Allah, forgetting that even the Prophet ﷺ was told to strive but hope for mercy? Is your worship driven by expectation of reward or by love and submission?
?
Nestorius manipulated the Gospels to fit his opinion. When you read the Quran, do you ever find yourself interpreting verses in a way that softens a command you find difficult? Be specific: what is one verse you have rationalized away rather than obeyed?

Sects and Disagreements
intermediate

The Logical Refutation of Trinitarian Claims
Baqillani refutes the Jacobite/Nestorian and Melkite positions using logical contradictions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's logical arguments that expose contradictions in both the Jacobite/Nestorian and the Melkite positions.

Core Idea
If the essence is the hypostases, it must be both undifferentiated and differentiated; if the essence is other than the hypostases, there are four gods or a redundant fourth.

After detailing the various Trinitarian beliefs, Baqillani delivers the crushing logical blow. He first refutes the Jacobite/Nestorian position by showing that if the essence is the hypostases, then the essence would have contradictory attributes. He then refutes the Melkite position by arguing that if the essence is distinct from the hypostases, either there are four gods or the essence is redundant. Both alternatives are absurd.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation of Jacobites/Nestorians
Read the argument: if the essence is the hypostases and the hypostases are differentiated, counted, and one unites with humanity, then the essence must be both undifferentiated and differentiated — a contradiction.
Notice the use of the question 'Afalaysa...' to elicit agreement.
2
Read the refutation of Melkites
If the essence is other than the hypostases, then the three hypostases plus the essence make four gods. If they claim only the hypostases are gods, then the essence is redundant.
Baqillani shows that the Melkite position collapses into polytheism or nonsense.
3
Reflect on the method
Baqillani uses pure logic without relying on scripture. He forces the opponent into impossible positions.
This is a classic kalam argumentative technique.

Source Text

الأقانيم له أقانيم : أهو عندكم الأقانيم أم غيرها؟ فإن قالت اليعقوبية والنسطورية : ليس الجوهر بغير الأقانيم ، قيل : أفليس الجوهر غير مختلف من حيث كان جوهراً ومن حيث لم يكن معدوداً ومن حيث لم تكن له خواص متباينة المعنى ؟
اليعقوبية: وهم أصحاب يعقوب. قالوا بالأقانيم الثلاثة، إلا أنهم قالوا : انقلبت الكلمة لحماً ودماً، فصار الإله هو المسيح. وهو الظاهر بجسده، بل هو هو. وعنهم أخبرنا القرآن الكريم لقد كفر الذين قالوا إن الله هو المسيح ابن مريم فمنهم من قال: إن المسيح الله تعالى. ومنهم من قال ظهر اللاهوت بالناسوت فصار ناسوت المسيح مظهر الجوهرة، لا على طريق حلول جزء فيه، ولا على سبيل اتحاد الكلمة التي هي في حكم الصفة بل صار هو هو. وهذا كما يقال ظهر الملك بصورة إنسان، أو ظهر الشيطان بصورة حيوان وزعم قوم من اليعقوبية أن الكلمة لم تأخذ من مريم شيئاً، ولكنها مرت بها كالماء بالميزاب وما ظهر بها من شخص المسيح في الأعين فهو كالخيال والصورة في المرآة وإلا فما كان جسماً متجسماً كثيفاً في الحقيقة. وكذلك القتل والصلب وإنما وقع على الخيال والحسبان، وهؤلاء يقال لهم الإليانية وهم قوم بالشام واليمن وأرمينية قالوا : إنما صلب الإله أحلنا من حتى يخلصنا. وزعم بعضهم أن الكلمة كانت تدخل جسم المسيح عليه السلام أحياناً، فتصدر عنه الآيات من إحياء الموتى، وإبراء الأكمه والأبرص وتفارقه في بعض الأوقات فترد عليه الآلام والأوجاع.
النسطورية: أصحاب نسطور وقد تصرف في الأناجيل بحكم رأيه وإضافته إليهم إضافة المعتزلة إلى هذه الشريعة قال : إن الله تعالى واحد ذو أقانيم ثلاثة الوجود والعلم والحياة، وهذه الأقانيم ليست زائدة على الذات ولا هي هو واتحدت الكلمة بجسد عيسى عليه السلام، لا على طريقة الامتزاج كما قالت الملكانية، ولا على طريقة الظهورية كما قالت اليعقوبية ولكن كإشراق الشمس في كوة على بلورة، وكظهور النقش في الشمع إذا طبع الخاتم وأشبه المذاهب بمذهب نسطور في الأقانيم : أحوال أبي هاشم من المعتزلة، فإنه يثبت خواص مختلفة لشيء واحد ويعني بقوله واحد يعني الإله . قال : هو واحد بالجوهر. أي ليس هو مركبا من جنسين بل هو بسيط وواحد. ويعني بالحياة والعلم اقنومين جوهرين، أي أصلين مبدأين للعالم. ثم فسر العلم بالنطق والكلمة . ويرجع منتهى كلامه إلى إثبات كونه تعالى موجوداً، حياً، ناطقاً كما تقول الفلاسفة في أحد الإنسان إلا أن هذه المعاني تتغاير في الإنسان ككونه جوهراً مركباً. وهو جوهر بسيط غير مركب. ومن النسطورية قوم يقال لهم المصلين قالوا في المسيح مثل ما قال نسطور إلا أنهم قالوا : إذا اجتهد الرجل في العبادة، وترك التغذي باللحم والدسم، ورفض الشهوات الحيوانية والنفسانية، تصفي جوهره حتى يبلغ ملكوت السموات ويرى الله تعالى جهرة وينكشف له ما في الغيب فلا تخفى عليه خافية الأرض ولا في السماء. ومن النسطورية من ينفي التشبيه، ويثبت القول بالقدر خيره وشره من العبد كما قالت القدرية.
ثم قيل لهم : أفليس الأقانيم مختلفة من حيث هي خواص متباينة المعنى، ومن حيث هي معدودة، ومن حيث هي أقانيم، ومن حيث أن الابن منها تدرع واتحد بجسد المسيح عليه السلام دون الرُّوح ؟ فإن قالوا : نعم، ولا بد من ذلك، قيل لهم : فإذا كان الجوهر هو الأقانيم والأقانيم مختلفة معدودة متباينة في الاختصاص، ومنها المتحد وهي نفس الجوهر، فنفس الجوهر إذاً مختلفة معدودة متباينة متحدة بناسوت المسيح عليه السلام فيجب أن يكون نفس الجوهر الذي ليس بمعدودٍ ولا مختلف ولا متحدٍ ولا متباين المعنى هو نفس المختلف المعدود المتباين المعنى المتحد؛ وهذا جهل ممن صار إليه وليس ذلك قولهم في الجوهر ؛ ولا خلاص لهم منه.
فإن قالت الملكية منهم، وهم الروم : إن الجوهر غير الأقانيم، قيل لهم : فإذا كان الجوهر إلها، والأقانيم الثلاثة آلهة وهي غيره، فالآلهة إذاً أربعة : جوهر وثلاثة أقانيم غيره؛ وهذا يبطل قولكم بالتثليث. وإن قالوا : الآلهة ثلاثة أقانيم، والرابع جوهر ليس بإله غير الثلاثة، قيل لهم : فلا فرق إذاً بين قول الأقانيم ثلاثة ولا جوهر هناك يجمعها وتكون له، وبين قول : إن هناك ثلاثة أقانيم وجوهراً جامعاً لها؛ فيجب أن يكون وجود الرابع كعدمه وإثباته كنفيه؛ وهذا جهل ممن صار إليه.
The hypostases have hypostases: Is it in your view that they are the hypostases or other than them? If the Jacobites and Nestorians say: The essence is not other than the hypostases, it is said: Is not the essence non-different in that it is an essence, and in that it is not counted, and in that it does not have mutually distinct properties? The Jacobites: They are the followers of Jacob. They affirmed the three hypostases, except that they said: The Word turned into flesh and blood, so God became the Messiah. He is apparent with His body, rather He is He. And from them the noble Quran told us: 'Certainly disbelieved those who said that God is the Messiah, son of Mary.' Some of them said: The Messiah is God Almighty. Some of them said: The divinity appeared in the humanity, so the humanity of the Messiah became a manifestation of the essence, not by way of indwelling of a part in it, nor by way of union of the Word which is in the status of an attribute, but He became He. This is like saying the king appears in the form of a man, or the devil appears in the form of an animal. And a group of the Jacobites claimed that the Word did not take anything from Mary, but it passed through her like water through a spout, and what appeared of the person of the Messiah in the eyes is like an illusion and an image in a mirror; otherwise, it was not a thick, embodied body in reality. Likewise, the killing and crucifixion only occurred upon illusion and imagination. These are called the Elianites, and they are a people in Syria, Yemen, and Armenia. They said: The god was crucified to atone for us so that He might save us. And some of them claimed that the Word used to enter the body of the Messiah, peace be upon him, sometimes, and miracles would issue from him, such as reviving the dead, healing the blind and leper, and it would leave him at other times, so pains and ailments would return to him. The Nestorians: They are the followers of Nestorius, who manipulated the Gospels according to his opinion and added to them as the Mu'tazilites added to this Sharia. He said: God Almighty is one, possessing three hypostases: existence, knowledge, and life. These hypostases are not additional to the essence nor are they identical with it. The Word united with the body of Jesus, peace be upon him, not by way of mixing as the Melkites said, nor by way of manifestation as the Jacobites said, but like the shining of the sun through a skylight onto a crystal, and like the appearance of an engraving in wax when stamped with a seal. The school of Nestorius regarding the hypostases resembles the states of Abu Hashim from the Mu'tazilites, for he affirms different properties for one thing. By 'one' he means God. He said: He is one in essence, meaning He is not composed of two kinds but is simple and one. He means by life and knowledge two essential hypostases, i.e., two origins, two principles of the world. Then he interpreted knowledge as speech and word. The conclusion of his speech returns to affirming that He, exalted, is existent, living, speaking, as the philosophers say about any human, except that these meanings differ in the human as he is a composite essence. He is a simple essence, not composite. Among the Nestorians are a people called the Prayers, who said about the Messiah like what Nestorius said, except they said: When a man strives in worship, abandons eating meat and fat, and rejects animal and soulful desires, his essence becomes purified until he reaches the kingdom of the heavens and sees God Almighty openly, and what is in the unseen is revealed to him, so no hidden thing on earth or in heaven is hidden from him. Among the Nestorians are those who negate anthropomorphism and affirm the doctrine of predestination, its good and evil, from the servant, as the Qadariyya said. Then it was said to them: Are not the hypostases different in that they are mutually distinct properties, and in that they are counted, and in that they are hypostases, and in that the Son among them put on armor and united with the body of the Messiah, peace be upon him, without the Spirit? If they say: Yes, and that is necessary, it is said to them: If the essence is the hypostases, and the hypostases are different, counted, distinct in specificity, and among them is the one that united, and it is the essence itself, then the essence itself is therefore different, counted, distinct, united with the humanity of the Messiah, peace be upon him. So it must be that the essence itself which is not counted, not different, not united, and not of distinct meaning is the same as the different, counted, distinct-in-meaning, united one. This is ignorance on the part of whoever holds it, and that is not their statement about the essence, and there is no escape from it for them. If the Melkites among them, who are the Romans, say: The essence is other than the hypostases, it is said to them: If the essence is a god, and the three hypostases are gods and are other than it, then the gods are four: an essence and three hypostases other than it. This invalidates your doctrine of trinity. And if they say: The gods are three hypostases, and the fourth is an essence that is not a god other than the three, it is said to them: There is no difference then between saying 'three hypostases and no essence that encompasses them and belongs to them' and saying 'there are three hypostases and an encompassing essence for them'. So the existence of the fourth must be like its non-existence, and its affirmation like its negation. This is ignorance on the part of whoever holds it.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Christian Trinitarian doctrines concerning the hypostases (aqanim) and the essence (jawhar). Baqillani begins by posing a key question: In your view, are the hypostases identical to the essence or distinct from it? He then addresses two main positions. First, the Jacobites and Nestorians claim that the essence is not other than the hypostases. Baqillani first provides a detailed account of each sect's beliefs: the Jacobites hold that the Word became flesh and that the divine and human are united in such a way that the divine is manifested through the human, while the Nestorians affirm three hypostases (existence, knowledge, life) and a union of the Word with the body of Jesus like the shining of sunlight or the impression of a seal. He then proceeds to the logical refutation. He asks: Is not the essence non-differentiated, non-countable, without mutually distinct properties? They must agree. Then he asks: Are not the hypostases different (as distinct properties), countable, hypostases, and the Son is said to have taken flesh and united with Christ to the exclusion of the Spirit? They agree again. Then follows the contradiction: If the essence is the hypostases, and the hypostases are different, countable, distinct, and one of them is united, then the essence itself must possess all those attributes (different, countable, distinct, united). Yet the essence is also supposed to be without these attributes (non-differentiated, non-countable, etc.). Thus the same entity would have contradictory properties, which is absurd. Hence their position is untenable. Second, Baqillani addresses the Melkites (the Romans) who say the essence is other than the hypostases. If the essence is a god and the three hypostases are gods distinct from it, then there would be four gods, contradicting the doctrine of trinity. If they instead claim that only the three hypostases are gods and the fourth (the essence) is not a god, then that essence is redundant and adds nothing; its existence is equivalent to non-existence. Thus their view also collapses. The passage demonstrates Baqillani's method of exposing internal inconsistencies in opposing doctrines without relying on scriptural authority.

التثليث
الرد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think Trinitarian doctrines are beyond rational critique and can only be accepted by faith.
Correction: Baqillani shows that Trinitarian claims lead to straightforward logical contradictions, making them untenable even without appealing to revelation.

Checkpoint
What is the logical consequence if the Melkites claim that the essence is other than the hypostases?
A) There are exactly three gods.
B) There are four gods or the essence is redundant.
C) The hypostases become the essence.
D) The Trinity remains intact.

Key Takeaway
Trinitarian doctrines, whether claiming identity or distinction between essence and hypostases, lead to logical absurdities: either contradiction or polytheism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson exposes logical contradictions in a widely held doctrine. Have you ever accepted a belief—religious or otherwise—on authority alone without testing its internal consistency? Will you commit to examining your own convictions with the same rigorous logic Baqillani applied here?
?
Baqillani's arguments require no scripture, only reason. Do you trust that your intellect is sufficient to discern truth in matters of faith? Or do you fear that rational scrutiny might undermine your beliefs? Pledge to use your mind fearlessly for the sake of truth.
?
The Melkite position reduces their fourth essence to a meaningless redundancy. Are there practices or beliefs in your life that you maintain but which are functionally redundant? What would it cost you to strip them away? Ask Allah for the courage to abandon what is superfluous and embrace pure tawheed.

Refutation of Essence-Hypostases Identity
Baqillani refutes the identity of essence and hypostases via contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why identifying the divine essence with the hypostases leads to an untenable contradiction regarding divine simplicity.

Core Idea
If the essence is the hypostases, it becomes multiple and changing — contradicting divine oneness.

Baqillani begins by engaging the Christian claim that the divine essence (al-jawhar) is identical with the three hypostases. Through a simple yet devastating line of questioning, he exposes the logical outcome of this identification: if the hypostases are distinct, counted, and one of them united with Christ's body, then the essence itself must share these properties, contradicting its supposed unity and immutability.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Christian claim
Read the opening question: do the hypostases have distinct meanings? The Christian affirms. Note that this sets up the trap.
The opponent agrees the hypostases are distinct properties.
2
Follow the logical consequences
If the essence is the hypostases, then the essence inherits all their attributes: being multiple, counted, and even uniting with Christ. Trace how Baqillani draws this conclusion.
3
Recognize the contradiction
The essence is supposed to be one, uncounted, and unchanging. The conclusion that it is multiple and united with Christ creates an absurdity. This shows the identity claim is false.
The contradiction is between divine simplicity and the multiplicity of the hypostases.

خواص متباينة المعنى؟ فإن قالوا: أجل، وهو قولهم، قيل لهم: أفليس الأقانيم مختلفة من حيث هي خواص متباينة المعنى، ومن حيث هي معدودة، ومن حيث هي أقانيم، ومن حيث أن الابن منها تدرع واتحد بجسد المسيح عليه السلام دون الروح؟ فإن قالوا: نعم، ولا بد من ذلك، قيل لهم: فإذا كان الجوهر هو الأقانيم والأقانيم مختلفة معدودة متباينة في الاختصاص، ومنها المتحد، وهي نفس الجوهر، فنفس الجوهر إذاً مختلفة معدودة متباينة متحدة بناسوت المسيح عليه السلام فيجب أن يكون نفس الجوهر الذي ليس بمعدود ولا مختلف ولا متحد ولا متباين المعنى هو نفس المختلف المعدود المتباين المعنى المتحد؛ وهذا جهل ممن صار إليه وليس ذلك قولهم في الجوهر؛ ولا خلاص لهم منه. فإن قالت الملكية منهم، وهم الروم: إن الجوهر غير الأقانيم، قيل لهم: فإذا كان الجوهر إلها، والأقانيم الثلاثة آلهة وهي غيره، فالآلهة إذا أربعة: جوهر وثلاثة أقانيم غيره؛ وهذا يبطل قولكم بالتثليث. وإن قالوا: الآلهة ثلاثة أقانيم، والرابع جوهر ليس بإله غير الثلاثة قيل لهم: فلا فرق إذاً بين قول الأقانيم ثلاثة ولا جوهر هناك يجمعها وتكون له، وبين قول: إن هناك ثلاثة أقانيم وجوهراً جامعاً لها؛ فيجب أن يكون وجود الرابع كعدمه وإثباته كنفيه؛ وهذا جهل ممن صار إليه. ويقال لهم: إن جاز أن يكون الرابع مع الثلاثة ثلاثة فقط، فما أنكرتم أن يكون الروح والعلم مع الإله الموجود واحداً فقط وأن يكون أقنوماً واحداً ولا يكون الثاني والثالث شيئاً يزيد على الواحد كما لم يكن الرابع شيئاً يزيد على الثالث فتكون الثلاثة الأقانيم هي جوهر واحد كما كانت الأربعة التي منها الجوهر ثلاثة؛ ولا جواب عن ذلك.
Properties with distinct meanings? If they say: Yes, that is their statement, it is said to them: Are not the hypostases different in that they are properties with distinct meanings, and in that they are counted, and in that they are hypostases, and in that the Son from them put on and united with the body of the Messiah peace be upon him without the Spirit? If they say: Yes, necessarily, it is said to them: If the essence is the hypostases and the hypostases are different, counted, distinct in specification, and among them is the one that united, and they are the essence itself, then the essence itself is therefore different, counted, distinct, united with the humanity of the Messiah peace be upon him. So it must be that the essence itself which is not counted, not different, not united, and not distinct in meaning is the same as the different, counted, distinct in meaning, united one; this is ignorance on the part of whoever holds it, and that is not their statement about the essence; and there is no escape from it. If the Melkites among them, the Romans, say: The essence is other than the hypostases, it is said to them: If the essence is a god, and the three hypostases are gods and are other than it, then the gods are four: an essence and three hypostases other than it; and this invalidates your statement of trinity. And if they say: The gods are three hypostases, and the fourth is an essence not a god other than the three, it is said to them: There is no difference then between the statement that there are three hypostases and no essence that gathers them and belongs to them, and the statement that there are three hypostases and a comprehensive essence for them; so it must be that the existence of the fourth is like its non-existence and its affirmation like its negation; this is ignorance on the part of whoever holds it. And it is said to them: If it is permissible that the fourth with the three is only three, then why do you deny that the Spirit and Knowledge with the existing God are only one and that it is one hypostasis, and the second and third are not something additional to the one, just as the fourth was not something additional to the third, so that the three hypostases are one essence just as the four, including the essence, were three; and there is no answer to that.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Christian claim that the divine essence (جوهر) is identical with the three hypostases (أقانيم). The argument proceeds stepwise:
1. The author begins by asking whether the hypostases are distinct properties. The opponent agrees that they have distinct meanings, are counted, and that the Son uniquely united with Christ's body. From this, Baqillani draws the consequence: if the essence is the hypostases, then the essence itself must share these properties—it becomes multiple, distinct, and subject to union with Christ. But the essence is supposed to be one, uncounted, and unchanging. Thus the identification leads to a contradiction.
2. Then the author considers the Melkite position that the essence is distinct from the hypostases. If the essence is God and the three hypostases are gods distinct from it, then there are four gods, contradicting trinity.
3. If they avoid this by saying the fourth (the essence) is not a god, then the essence is superfluous, and its existence or non-existence makes no difference—another absurdity.
4. Finally, Baqillani argues that if the fourth can be counted as three when combined with the three hypostases, then by analogy the Spirit and Knowledge could be one hypostasis, reducing the Trinity to a single hypostasis, which undermines their doctrine. The passage concludes that there is no answer to this refutation.

Key Terms
جوهر
أقانيم
متباينة
معدودة
ناسوت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hypostases are merely modes or properties of the divine essence, so identity does not imply multiplicity.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the hypostases are considered distinct and counted, so if they are the essence, the essence becomes multiple—contradicting divine simplicity.

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani conclude if the essence is identical with the hypostases?
A) The essence remains one and simple.
B) The essence becomes multiple and united with Christ.
C) The hypostases become one.
D) The Trinity is preserved.

Key Takeaway
Identifying the divine essence with the hypostases forces the essence to become multiple and mutable, which is impossible for God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held a belief about God that, upon reflection, led to a contradiction with His oneness? What did you do to resolve it? Now, examine your current understanding: Are there any subtle compromises on tawhid you need to correct today?
?
The passage shows that even well-intentioned descriptions of God can inadvertently produce contradictions. When you speak about God's attributes, do you allow Him to be as He described Himself, or do you impose human categories? Will you commit to studying the Qur'an and Sunnah with a scholar to purify your understanding?
?
Baqillani's argument forces the opponent to face the logical consequences of their claim. Are you willing to subject your own theological positions to the same rigorous scrutiny? What is one belief you hold that you have not critically examined? Set a time to investigate it thoroughly with a reliable source.

intermediate
6 min
Refutation of Essence-Hypostases Distinction
Baqillani refutes the distinction of essence and hypostases via dilemmas and counting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why distinguishing the essence from the hypostases leads to either four gods or a superfluous fourth, and why the counting argument undermines the Trinity.

Core Idea
If essence is distinct from hypostases, either four gods or a useless fourth entity results.

Baqillani now turns to the Melkite (Roman Christian) position that the divine essence is distinct from the hypostases. He presents a dilemma: if the essence is God and the hypostases are gods, then there are four gods; if the essence is not god, then it is redundant. Finally, he uses a clever counting argument to show that the Trinity could be reduced to a single hypostasis, exposing the inconsistency of their doctrine.

Guided Path
1
Examine the Melkite distinction
Read the dilemma: if essence is distinct and both are gods, there are four gods; if essence is not god, it is unnecessary.
The Melkites claim essence ≠ hypostases.
2
Analyze the counting argument
The fourth (essence) with the three hypostases is still considered three? Follow the logic: if the fourth adds nothing, then by analogy, the Spirit and Knowledge could be one hypostasis, reducing the Trinity to one.
This shows the arbitrariness of their enumeration.
3
Appreciate the final conclusion
The argument leaves the Christian with no answer, exposing the incoherence of the Trinity doctrine.

خواص متباينة المعنى؟ فإن قالوا: أجل، وهو قولهم، قيل لهم: أفليس الأقانيم مختلفة من حيث هي خواص متباينة المعنى، ومن حيث هي معدودة، ومن حيث هي أقانيم، ومن حيث أن الابن منها تدرع واتحد بجسد المسيح عليه السلام دون الروح؟ فإن قالوا: نعم، ولا بد من ذلك، قيل لهم: فإذا كان الجوهر هو الأقانيم والأقانيم مختلفة معدودة متباينة في الاختصاص، ومنها المتحد، وهي نفس الجوهر، فنفس الجوهر إذاً مختلفة معدودة متباينة متحدة بناسوت المسيح عليه السلام فيجب أن يكون نفس الجوهر الذي ليس بمعدود ولا مختلف ولا متحد ولا متباين المعنى هو نفس المختلف المعدود المتباين المعنى المتحد؛ وهذا جهل ممن صار إليه وليس ذلك قولهم في الجوهر؛ ولا خلاص لهم منه. فإن قالت الملكية منهم، وهم الروم: إن الجوهر غير الأقانيم، قيل لهم: فإذا كان الجوهر إلها، والأقانيم الثلاثة آلهة وهي غيره، فالآلهة إذا أربعة: جوهر وثلاثة أقانيم غيره؛ وهذا يبطل قولكم بالتثليث. وإن قالوا: الآلهة ثلاثة أقانيم، والرابع جوهر ليس بإله غير الثلاثة قيل لهم: فلا فرق إذاً بين قول الأقانيم ثلاثة ولا جوهر هناك يجمعها وتكون له، وبين قول: إن هناك ثلاثة أقانيم وجوهراً جامعاً لها؛ فيجب أن يكون وجود الرابع كعدمه وإثباته كنفيه؛ وهذا جهل ممن صار إليه. ويقال لهم: إن جاز أن يكون الرابع مع الثلاثة ثلاثة فقط، فما أنكرتم أن يكون الروح والعلم مع الإله الموجود واحداً فقط وأن يكون أقنوماً واحداً ولا يكون الثاني والثالث شيئاً يزيد على الواحد كما لم يكن الرابع شيئاً يزيد على الثالث فتكون الثلاثة الأقانيم هي جوهر واحد كما كانت الأربعة التي منها الجوهر ثلاثة؛ ولا جواب عن ذلك.
Properties with distinct meanings? If they say: Yes, that is their statement, it is said to them: Are not the hypostases different in that they are properties with distinct meanings, and in that they are counted, and in that they are hypostases, and in that the Son from them put on and united with the body of the Messiah peace be upon him without the Spirit? If they say: Yes, necessarily, it is said to them: If the essence is the hypostases and the hypostases are different, counted, distinct in specification, and among them is the one that united, and they are the essence itself, then the essence itself is therefore different, counted, distinct, united with the humanity of the Messiah peace be upon him. So it must be that the essence itself which is not counted, not different, not united, and not distinct in meaning is the same as the different, counted, distinct in meaning, united one; this is ignorance on the part of whoever holds it, and that is not their statement about the essence; and there is no escape from it. If the Melkites among them, the Romans, say: The essence is other than the hypostases, it is said to them: If the essence is a god, and the three hypostases are gods and are other than it, then the gods are four: an essence and three hypostases other than it; and this invalidates your statement of trinity. And if they say: The gods are three hypostases, and the fourth is an essence not a god other than the three, it is said to them: There is no difference then between the statement that there are three hypostases and no essence that gathers them and belongs to them, and the statement that there are three hypostases and a comprehensive essence for them; so it must be that the existence of the fourth is like its non-existence and its affirmation like its negation; this is ignorance on the part of whoever holds it. And it is said to them: If it is permissible that the fourth with the three is only three, then why do you deny that the Spirit and Knowledge with the existing God are only one and that it is one hypostasis, and the second and third are not something additional to the one, just as the fourth was not something additional to the third, so that the three hypostases are one essence just as the four, including the essence, were three; and there is no answer to that.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Christian claim that the divine essence (جوهر) is identical with the three hypostases (أقانيم). The argument proceeds stepwise:
1. The author begins by asking whether the hypostases are distinct properties. The opponent agrees that they have distinct meanings, are counted, and that the Son uniquely united with Christ's body. From this, Baqillani draws the consequence: if the essence is the hypostases, then the essence itself must share these properties—it becomes multiple, distinct, and subject to union with Christ. But the essence is supposed to be one, uncounted, and unchanging. Thus the identification leads to a contradiction.
2. Then the author considers the Melkite position that the essence is distinct from the hypostases. If the essence is God and the three hypostases are gods distinct from it, then there are four gods, contradicting trinity.
3. If they avoid this by saying the fourth (the essence) is not a god, then the essence is superfluous, and its existence or non-existence makes no difference—another absurdity.
4. Finally, Baqillani argues that if the fourth can be counted as three when combined with the three hypostases, then by analogy the Spirit and Knowledge could be one hypostasis, reducing the Trinity to a single hypostasis, which undermines their doctrine. The passage concludes that there is no answer to this refutation.

Key Terms
جوهر
أقانيم
تثليث
ملكية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hypostases are distinct but the essence is not a fourth god, so trinity is preserved.
Correction: Baqillani shows that if the essence is not god, it is redundant, and the counting argument further undermines the threeness.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if the Melkites say the essence is other than the hypostases and both are gods?
A) There are three gods.
B) There are four gods.
C) The essence is not god.
D) The hypostases are not gods.

Key Takeaway
Distinguishing essence from hypostases leads to either polytheism or a meaningless fourth entity, and the counting argument exposes logical inconsistency.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just seen how logical reasoning exposes the incoherence of dividing Allah's oneness. Is there any area of your own belief—perhaps a comfortable assumption or a practice you have not examined—where you hold a contradiction or a subtle distinction that undermines pure tawheed? What would it take for you to submit completely to the absolute oneness of Allah, even if it requires you to abandon a long-held idea?
?
The Melkites clung to a doctrine that appeared to protect their concept of God but led to logical absurdity. In your own life, are there comfortable beliefs or habits that, when honestly examined in light of the Quran and Sunnah, contradict the clear teaching of tawheed? How will you re-align your heart and actions this week?
?
Baqillani's argument leaves 'no answer' to the counting analogy. If you were challenged on a core aspect of your faith—such as the justice of Allah, the nature of divine decree, or the reality of resurrection—would you have a reasoned defense rooted in revelation and sound reasoning, or a blind spot you have avoided? What will you do to be prepared to give an answer for the hope within you, not just with words but with conviction?

Baqillani's Refutation of Tritheism
Baqillani refutes the Nestorian and Jacobite statement that each hypostasis is God yet they are one.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Christian Trinity as described by the Nestorians and Jacobites is logically self-contradictory according to Baqillani.

Core Idea
Three gods cannot be one God without contradiction.

In this brief but decisive passage, Imam Baqillani takes aim at the Christian doctrine of the Trinity as formulated by the Nestorians and Jacobites. He points out the immediate logical problem: if each hypostasis (Father, Son, Spirit) is fully God, then there are three gods. The claim that they are one God is then meaningless. This lesson will unpack that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic and English side by side to grasp the concise argument.
2
Identify the claim being refuted
Note the exact statement: Father is God, Son is God, Spirit is God, yet they are one. This is the target.
3
Understand the logical contradiction
Baqillani reasons that if each is God, then there are three gods. Calling them one contradicts the assignment of divinity to each.
4
Ask why this refutation matters
Consider how Baqillani uses simple logic (non-contradiction) to challenge a foundational Christian belief.
This shows the kalam approach of holding claims to rational consistency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك يقال لهم وللنسطورية واليعقوبية في قولهم: «إن الأب إله وإن الابن إله وإن الروح إله وإن الآلهة مع ذلك واحد»؛ لأنه إذا كان كل واحد منهم ثلاثة آلهة؛ ولا معنى لقولهم إله واحد، وهم قد جعلوا الإلهية لكل واحد منهم.
And likewise it is said to them and to the Nestorians and Jacobites regarding their statement: 'Indeed the Father is God, and the Son is God, and the Spirit is God, and the gods with that are one'; because if each one of them is three gods, there is no meaning to their statement 'one God', while they have assigned divinity to every single one of them.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a brief refutation of the Nestorian and Jacobite doctrine that each of the three hypostases—Father, Son, and Holy Spirit—is God, yet they are one God. Baqillani points out the logical contradiction: if each hypostasis is individually God, then there are three gods. To then claim that these three gods are one God is meaningless because 'one God' cannot consist of three distinct divine individuals. The assignment of divinity to each hypostasis results in tritheism, not monotheism.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may assume the Christian Trinity is a mystery beyond logic that cannot be rationally assessed.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the Trinity as described (each hypostasis fully God yet one God) is a straightforward logical contradiction that violates the principle of non-contradiction.

Checkpoint

A) It implies three gods, not one.
B) It denies the divinity of the Son.
C) It implies the essence is divisible.
D) It confuses the hypostases with properties.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani demonstrates that claiming each hypostasis is God leads logically to tritheism, not monotheism.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Now ask yourself: In your own life, are there any contradictions between what you claim to believe and what your actions or assumptions imply? Where do you say 'la ilaha illallah' but act as if something else shares in His exclusivity? Identify one area and commit to correcting it this week.
?
Baqillani exposes the absurdity of claiming three are one while assigning divinity to each. How often do you settle for comfortable contradictions in your own faith—holding onto beliefs that logic or scripture refute, just because they feel familiar? Can you name one inherited assumption about God that you have not critically examined? What step will you take to verify it?
?
The opponents' statement 'the gods are one' is labeled meaningless (لا معنى). Consider your own worship: Are there any acts you perform that you call 'for Allah alone' but in your heart you seek recognition from others or rely on your own strength? Will you repent and realign your intention before your next prayer?

Baqillani's Dilemma: Essence and Hypostases
Baqillani poses a dilemma to the Melkites about essence and hypostases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses a strategic question to force a logical dilemma on the Melkite Trinity doctrine.

Core Idea
A well-crafted question can expose internal contradictions in a rival theology.

Baqillani poses a concise but devastating dilemma to the Melkites. By asking whether the divine essence is similar or different from the three hypostases, he sets up a logical trap. No matter which answer they give, it leads to an inconsistency with their own premises. This lesson examines the structure of this kind of argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Notice the structure of the question and the two options presented.
The passage is incomplete; the response is cut off.
2
Identify the two options
Baqillani offers two possibilities: the essence is either similar (موافق) or different (مخالف) from the hypostases. Understand what each option implies.
3
Consider the logical consequences
Think about what follows if they say 'similar' — the essence would share attributes with the hypostases, implying multiplicity in the essence. If 'different' — the essence is disconnected from the hypostases, contradicting their unity.
4
Speculate on the missing part
The text cuts off after 'قيل لهم' (it is said to them). Imagine what Baqillani would argue next based on the dilemma. How would he refute each answer?
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text

مسألة أخرى على الملكية يقال لهم: خبرونا عن الجوهر الذي هو عندكم غير الأقانيم: أهو ذلك مخالف لها أو موافق لها؟ فإن قالوا: إنه موافق لها قيل لهم:
Another question against the Melkites. It is said to them: Inform us about the essence which with you is other than the hypostases: is it that which is different from them or similar to them? If they say: It is similar to them, it is said to them:
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage presents a new question directed at the Melkites, who hold that the divine essence (جوهر) is distinct from the three hypostases (أقانيم). Baqillani asks: Is this essence similar (موافق) or different (مخالف) from the hypostases? The question is designed to force a dilemma. If they say it is similar, then the essence shares attributes with the hypostases, leading to plurality in the essence—contradicting its simplicity. If they say it is different, then the essence would be unlike the hypostases, raising questions about how it relates to them. Unfortunately, the page ends before presenting the full argument; the text cuts off at 'قيل لهم:' (it is said to them), so the intended refutation is not fully given in this window.

Refuting the Trinity: The Incoherence of Distinct Hypostases
Baqillani refutes the Trinity argument from hypostases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's logical refutation of the Christian Trinity doctrine, specifically how the claim that the hypostases add nothing to the divine essence undermines their distinctness.

Core Idea
If hypostases add nothing, why stop at three?

The Christian doctrine of the Trinity asserts that God exists as three distinct hypostases (Father, Son, Holy Spirit) sharing one essence. Baqillani challenges this by exposing a logical flaw: if the second and third hypostases add nothing to the first, then by the same logic a fourth would add nothing, and so on. This reveals the arbitrariness of the claim and refutes the notion of distinct hypostases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponent's claim
Read the passage and notice the claim that the Spirit and Knowledge are one with God as one hypostasis, and that the second and third add nothing to the first.
This is the Trinitarian position Baqillani is targeting.
2
Follow the reductio ad absurdum
Baqillani extends the logic: if the second and third add nothing, then a fourth would also add nothing. This leads to an absurd multiplication of hypostases.
The argument shows the criterion of 'adding nothing' does not limit hypostases to three.
3
Understand the conclusion
If three hypostases can be one essence because they add nothing, then four or more can also be one essence. The opponent's distinction collapses.
Baqillani asserts there is no answer to this refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أنكرتم أن يكون الرُّوح والعلم مع الإله الموجود واحداً فقط وأن يكون أقنوماً واحداً ولا يكون الثاني والثالث شيئاً يزيد على الواحد كما لم يكن الرابع شيئاً يزيد على الثالث فتكون الثلاثة الأقانيم هي جوهر واحد كما كانت الأربعة التي منها الجوهر ثلاثة ؛ ولا جواب عن ذلك.
You denied that the Spirit and the Knowledge are with the existing God one only, and that they are one hypostasis, and that the second and third are nothing that adds to the one, just as the fourth is nothing that adds to the third, so the three hypostases are one essence, just as the four, from which the essence is three; and there is no answer to that.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Christian doctrine of the Trinity. Baqillani argues against the claim that the Spirit and the Word (Knowledge) are one with God but are distinct hypostases. He uses a reductio ad absurdum: if the second and third hypostases add nothing to the first, then by the same logic a fourth would add nothing to the third, so you could have four hypostases and still call them one essence. This shows the incoherence of the Trinitarian claim that three distinct hypostases are one essence without any addition.

Key Terms
الرُّوح
العلم
الإله الموجود
أقنوم
جوهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Trinity is logically consistent because the three hypostases are distinct but one essence without addition.
Correction: Baqillani shows that if distinct hypostases add nothing to the essence, then any number of hypostases could be added, making the distinction arbitrary and incoherent.

Checkpoint

A) The second and third are equal to the first.
B) A fourth hypostasis would also add nothing, making the four one essence.
C) The essence is divisible into three parts.
D) The hypostases are not eternal.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes the Trinity by exposing that if distinct hypostases add nothing to the essence, there is no logical limit to their number, rendering the doctrine incoherent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

This argument exposes the incoherence of claiming distinct yet non-additive hypostases. Is there any area of your own belief where you accept contradictory propositions because they feel right? Will you examine them honestly today?

Refutation of Three Gods Claiming Oneness
Baqillani refutes the Trinity's claim of oneness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's logical argument against the Trinity's claim to be one God while each person is fully God.

Core Idea
If each person is fully God, they cannot be numerically one.

Baqillani addresses the Christian claim that Father, Son, and Spirit are each God yet still one God. He exposes a logical contradiction: if each is God, then there are three gods, not one. This passage is a classic refutation of Trinitarian theology from a monotheistic perspective.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Pay attention to the structure of the claim: 'The Father is God, the Son is God, the Spirit is God, and the God is with that one.' Note how Baqillani responds.
2
Identify the logical contradiction
Baqillani argues that if each person is God, then there are three gods. The phrase 'three gods' emphasizes the contradiction. Ask: Why does saying each is God make them three?
Consider the principle: if A=God and B=God and A≠B, then there are at least two gods unless they are identical in every way, which the Trinity denies.
3
Reflect on the meaning of 'one God'
Baqillani concludes that their statement 'one God' has no meaning because they have assigned divinity to each person. Reflect on how this argument targets the coherence of the Trinity.
This shows the Islamic critique that Trinitarian doctrine is logically inconsistent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك يقال لهم وللنسطورية واليعقوبية في قولهم: «إن الأب إله وإن الابن إله وإن الروح إله وإن الإله مع ذلك واحد» ؛ لأنه إذا كان كل واحد منهم ثلاثة آلهة ؛ ولا معنى لقولهم إله واحد ، وهم قد جعلوا الإلهية لكل واحد منهم.
And likewise it is said to them, and to the Nestorians and Jacobites, regarding their statement: 'The Father is God, and the Son is God, and the Spirit is God, and the God is with that one'; because if each one of them is three gods, there is no meaning to their statement 'one God', and they have made divinity for each one of them.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the common Christian statement that the Father, Son, and Holy Spirit are each God yet they are one God. Baqillani points out the contradiction: if each person is God, then there are three gods, not one. The phrase 'three gods' here is likely a rhetorical simplification—he means that attributing full divinity to each results in three distinct gods. He then notes that they have assigned divinity to each, undermining any claim to monotheism.

D) Because they believe in a hierarchy among the persons.
